resolution, the CCP promoted the terms [[Two Establishes and Two Safeguards]], calling the CCP to unite around and protect Xi's core status within the party.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Bandurski |first=David |date=8 February 2022 |title=Two Establishes |url=https://chinamediaproject.org/the_ccp_dictionary/two-establishes/ |access-date=12 August 2022 |website=China Media Project |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nThe [[20th National Congress of the Chinese Communist Party]], held between 16-22 October 2022, has overseen amendments in the [[Constitution of the Chinese Communist Party|CCP constitution]] and the re-election of Xi as general secretary of the CCP and chairman of the CMC for a third term, with the overall result of the Congress being further strengthening of Xi's power.<ref name=\":12\">{{Cite news |last1=Davidson |first1=Helen |last2=Graham-Harrison |first2=Emma |date=23 October 2022 |title=China's leader Xi Jinping secures third term and stacks inner circle with loyalists |work=[[The Guardian]] |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2022/oct/23/xi-jinping-to-rule-china-for-precedent-breaking-third-term |access-date=23 October 2022}}</ref> The newly amended CCP constitution included the terms two establishes and two safeguards, reinforcing Xi's power.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Ruwitch |first=John |date=23 October 2022 |title=China's Xi Jinping emerges from the Communist Party congress with dominance |language=en |work=[[NPR]] |url=https://www.npr.org/2022/10/23/1130771668/china-xi-jinping-third-term-leader |access-date=23 October 2022}}</ref> It also included concepts promoted by Xi like common prosperity, Chinese-style modernisation and whole-process people\u2019s democracy.<ref>{{Cite news |last= |date=22 October 2022 |title=Factbox: China's Communist Party amends its charter, strengthens Xi's power |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/china/chinas-communist-party-amends-its-charter-strengthens-xi-power-2022-10-22/ |access-date=23 October 2022}}</ref> The new Politburo Standing Committee elected just after the CCP Congress was filled almost completely with people close to Xi, with four out of the seven members of the previous PSC including premier [[Li Keqiang]] and CPPCC chairman [[Wang Yang (politician)|Wang Yang]] stepping down.<ref>{{Cite web |date=22 October 2022 |title=Shake-up at the top of China's Communist Party as Xi Jinping starts new term |url=https://www.scmp.com/news/china/politics/article/3196911/shake-top-chinas-communist-party-xi-jinping-starts-new-term |access-date=23 October 2022 |website=[[South China Morning Post]] |language=en}}</ref> [[Li Qiang]], a close Xi ally, became the second-ranking member of the PSC, and is expected to become premier in 2023.<ref name=\":12\" /> Other allies of Xi, including Cai Qi, [[Ding Xuexiang]] and [[Li Xi (politician)|Li Xi]] have also joined the PSC, and are expected to become first secretary of the [[Secretariat of the Chinese Communist Party|CCP Secretariat]], first [[Vice Premier of the People's Republic of China|vice premier]] and [[secretary of the Central Commission for Discipline Inspection]] respectively.<ref name=\":37\">{{Cite web |last1=Chun |first1=Han Wong |last2=Zhai |first2=Keith |date=23 October 2022 |title=China's Leaders: Xi Jinping and His Men |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/chinas-leaders-xi-jinping-and-his-men-11666538145 |access-date=23 October 2022 |website=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |language=en-US}}</ref> The only remaining members of the previous PSC except Xi were [[Zhao Leji]] and [[Wang Huning]], though their ranking and positions changed.<ref name=\":37\" /> Xi's re-election made him the first party leader since Mao Zedong to serve more than three terms, though Deng Xiaoping ruled the country informally for a longer period.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Wingfield-Hayes |first=Rupert |date=23 October 2022 |title=Xi Jinping's party is just getting started |language=en-GB |work=[[BBC News]] |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-china-63225277 |access-date=23 October 2022}}</ref>\n\n====Cult of personality====\n[[File:\u4e2d\u56fd\u8857\u5934\u51fa\u552e\u7684\u9762\u5b54\u53ef\u4ee5\u53d8\u6362\u7684\u6bdb\u6cfd\u4e1c\u548c\u4e60\u8fd1\u5e73\u50cf.png|thumb|[[Holography|Holographic]] portraits of [[Mao Zedong]] and Xi Jinping in a shop in China]]\n{{Main|Xi Jinping's cult of personality}}\n\nXi has had a [[cult of personality]] constructed around himself since entering office<ref name=\"EconomistCultPersonality\">{{Cite news |date=18 September 2014 |title=The power of Xi Jinping |newspaper=[[The Economist]] |url=https://www.economist.com/news/china/21618882-cult-personality-growing-around-chinas-president-what-will-he-do-his-political |url-status=live |url-access=subscription |access-date=20 September 2017 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171107055514/https://www.economist.com/news/china/21618882-cult-personality-growing-around-chinas-president-what-will-he-do-his-political |archive-date=7 November 2017}}</ref><ref name=\"ForeignPolicyCultPersonality\">{{Cite news |last1=Jiayang |first1=Fan |last2=Taisu |first2=Zhang |last3=Ying |first3=Zhu |date=8 March 2016 |title=Behind the Personality Cult of Xi Jinping |language=en-US |newspaper=[[Foreign Policy (magazine)|Foreign Policy]] |url=https://foreignpolicy.com/2016/03/08/the-personality-cult-of-xi-jinping-china-leader-communist-party/ |url-status=live |access-date=26 July 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190726173241/https://foreignpolicy.com/2016/03/08/the-personality-cult-of-xi-jinping-china-leader-communist-party/ |archive-date=26 July 2019}}</ref> with books, cartoons, pop songs and dance routines honouring his rule.<ref name=\"PhilGuard12\">{{Cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/sep/19/xi-jinping-does-china-truly-love-big-daddy-xi-or-fear-him|title=Xi Jinping: Does China truly love 'Big Daddy Xi' \u2013 or fear him?|last=Phillips|first=Tom|date=19 September 2015|work=[[The Guardian]]|access-date=31 August 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190427001038/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/sep/19/xi-jinping-does-china-truly-love-big-daddy-xi-or-fear-him|archive-date=27 April 2019|issn=0261-3077}}</ref> Following Xi's ascension to the [[leadership core]] of the CCP, he had been referred to as ''Xi Dada'' ({{zh|s=\u4e60\u5927\u5927|labels=no}}, Uncle or Papa Xi),<ref name=\"PhilGuard12\" /><ref>{{cite news |last1=Blanchard |first1=Ben |date=28 October 2016 |title=All hail the mighty uncle \u2013 Chinese welcome Xi as the 'core' |work=[[Reuters]] |publisher= |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-politics-xi-idUSKCN12S0AA |url-status=live |access-date=23 June 2018 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180624010629/https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-politics-xi-idUSKCN12S0AA |archive-date=24 June 2018}}</ref> though this stopped in April 2016.<ref>{{Cite news |date=28 April 2015 |title=Xi's Nickname Becomes Out of Bounds for China's Media |language=en |work=[[Bloomberg News]] |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2016-04-28/no-more-big-daddy-xi-as-china-s-spin-doctors-revise-playbook |access-date=11 August 2022}}</ref> The village of Liangjiahe, where Xi was sent to work, has become a \"modern-day shrine\" decorated with CCP propaganda and murals extolling the formative years of his life.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Rivers |first1=Matt |date=19 March 2018 |title=This entire Chinese village is a shrine to Xi Jinping |work=[[CNN]] |publisher= |url=https://edition.cnn.com/2018/03/19/asia/china-xi-jinping-village-intl/index.html |url-status=live |access-date=23 June 2018 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180624010733/https://edition.cnn.com/2018/03/19/asia/china-xi-jinping-village-intl/index.html |archive-date=24 June 2018}}</ref>\n\nThe [[Politburo of the Chinese Communist Party|CCP's Politburo]] named Xi Jinping ''lingxiu'' ({{zh|s=\u9886\u8896|labels=no}}), a reverent term for \"leader\" and a title previously only given to Mao Zedong and his immediate successor [[Hua Guofeng]].<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.scmp.com/news/china/policies-politics/article/2117421/xi-jinpings-latest-grandiose-title-aims-take|title=Why China is reviving Mao's grandiose title for Xi Jinping|last=Gan|first=Nectar|date=28 December 2017|newspaper=[[South China Morning Post]]|language=en|access-date=26 July 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.economist.com/china/2018/02/17/xi-jinping-is-no-longer-any-old-leader|title=Xi Jinping is no longer any old leader|date=17 February 2018|newspaper=[[The Economist]]|access-date=26 July 2019|issn=0013-0613}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |last1=Shepherd |first1=Christian |last2=Wen |first2=Philip |date=20 October 2017 |title=With tears and song, China welcomes Xi as great, wise leader |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |publisher= |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-congress-idUSKBN1CO0AV |access-date=26 July 2019}}</ref> He is also sometimes called the \"pilot at the helm\" ({{zh|s=\u9886\u822a\u638c\u8235|labels=no}}).<ref>{{Cite web |last=Qian |first=Gang |date=2 November 2020 |title=A Brief History of the Helmsmen |url=https://chinamediaproject.org/2020/11/02/a-brief-history-of-the-helmsman/ |access-date=16 August 2022 |website=China Media Project |language=en-US}}</ref> On 25 December 2019, the Politburo officially named Xi as \"People's Leader\" ({{zh|s=\u4eba\u6c11\u9886\u8896|labels=no|c=|t=|p=r\u00e9nm\u00edn l\u01d0ngxi\u00f9}}), a title only Mao had held previously.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://asia.nikkei.com/Editor-s-Picks/China-up-close/China-crowns-Xi-with-special-title-citing-rare-crisis|title=China crowns Xi with special title, citing rare crisis|last=Nakazawa|first=Katsuji|date=9 January 2020|work=[[Nikkei Asian Review]]|access-date=10 January 2020}}</ref>\n\n====Removal of term limits====\nIn March 2018, the party-controlled National People's Congress passed a set of constitutional amendments including removal of term limits for the president and vice president, the creation of a [[National Supervisory Commission]], as well as enhancing the central role of the CCP.<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy-defence/article/2134791/end-term-limits-top-may-be-start-global-backlash-china|title=End to term limits at top 'may be start of global backlash for China'|last1=Shi|first1=Jiangtao|date=26 February 2018|work=[[South China Morning Post]]|access-date=28 February 2018|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180227155138/http://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy-defence/article/2134791/end-term-limits-top-may-be-start-global-backlash-china|archive-date=27 February 2018|last2=Huang|first2=Kristin}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2018/mar/04/xi-jinping-from-president-to-china-new-dictator|title=Xi Jinping's power play: from president to China's new dictator?|last=Phillips|first=Tom|date=4 March 2018|website=[[The Guardian]]|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180304005848/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2018/mar/04/xi-jinping-from-president-to-china-new-dictator|archive-date=4 March 2018|access-date=4 March 2018}}</ref> On 17 March 2018, the Chinese legislature reappointed Xi as president, now without term limits; Wang Qishan was appointed vice president.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-parliament-xi/chinas-parliament-re-elects-xi-jinping-as-president-idUSKCN1GT03C|title=China's parliament re-elects Xi Jinping as president|last=Wen|first=Philip|date=17 March 2018|publisher=[[Reuters]]|access-date=17 March 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180317042406/https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-parliament-xi/chinas-parliament-re-elects-xi-jinping-as-president-idUSKCN1GT03C|archive-date=17 March 2018|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://apnews.com/78ea5b0646564a6eb98d9d20d5fbcbb6|title=Xi reappointed as China's president with no term limits|last1=Bodeen|first1=Christopher|date=17 March 2018|publisher=[[Associated Press]]|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180317190611/https://apnews.com/78ea5b0646564a6eb98d9d20d5fbcbb6|archive-date=17 March 2018|access-date=17 March 2018}}</ref> The following day, Li Keqiang was reappointed premier and longtime allies of Xi, [[Xu Qiliang]] and [[Zhang Youxia]], were voted in as vice-chairmen of the CMC.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.scmp.com/news/china/economy/article/2137707/li-keqiang-endorsed-chinas-premier-while-military-commission|title=Li Keqiang endorsed as China's premier; military leaders confirmed|last1=Zhou|first1=Xin|date=18 March 2018|newspaper=[[South China Morning Post]]|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190827155325/https://www.scmp.com/news/china/economy/article/2137707/li-keqiang-endorsed-chinas-premier-while-military-commission|archive-date=27 August 2019|access-date=7 September 2019}}</ref> Foreign minister [[Wang Yi (politician)|Wang Yi]] was promoted to [[State councillor (China)|state councillor]] and General [[Wei Fenghe]] was named [[Ministry of National Defense of the People's Republic of China|defence minister]].<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy-defence/article/2137769/china-promotes-foreign-minister-wang-yi-state|title=China's foreign minister gains power in new post as state councillor|last1=Ng|first1=Teddy|date=19 March 2018|newspaper=[[South China Morning Post]]|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190305121632/https://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy-defence/article/2137769/china-promotes-foreign-minister-wang-yi-state|archive-date=5 March 2019|access-date=7 September 2019}}</ref>\n\nAccording to the ''[[Financial Times]]'', Xi expressed his views of constitutional amendment at meetings with Chinese officials and foreign dignitaries. Xi explained the decision in terms of needing to align two more powerful posts\u2014general secretary of the CCP and chairman of the CMC\u2014which have no term limits. However, Xi did not say whether he intended to serve as party general secretary, CMC chairman and state president, for three or more terms.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.ft.com/content/2b449400-413a-11e8-803a-295c97e6fd0b|title=China's Xi Jinping says he is opposed to life-long rule|last1=Mitchell|first1=Tom|date=7 September 2019|newspaper=[[Financial Times]]|access-date=17 April 2018|quote=President insists term extension is necessary to align government and party posts|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180417192157/https://www.ft.com/content/2b449400-413a-11e8-803a-295c97e6fd0b|archive-date=17 April 2018|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\n===Economy and technology===\n{{Main|Economy of China}}\n\nXi was initially seen as a market reformist,<ref name=\":30\">{{Cite journal |last=Whyte |first=Martin K. |date=15 March 2021 |title=China's economic development history and Xi Jinping's \"China dream:\" an overview with personal reflections |url=https://doi.org/10.1080/21620555.2020.1833321 |journal=Chinese Sociological Review |volume=53 |issue=2 |pages=115\u2013134 |doi=10.1080/21620555.2020.1833321 |s2cid=228867589 |issn=2162-0555}}</ref> and the Third Plenum of the 18th Central Committee under him announced that \"market forces\" would begin to play a \"decisive\" role in allocating resources.<ref name=\"brook2\" /> This meant that the state would gradually reduce its involvement in the distribution of capital, and restructure [[state-owned enterprise]]s to allow further competition, potentially by attracting foreign and private sector players in industries that were previously highly regulated. This policy aimed to address the bloated state sector that had unduly profited from an earlier round of re-structuring by purchasing assets at below-market prices, assets that were no longer being used productively. However, by 2017, Xi's promise of economic reforms has been said to stall by experts.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Buckley |first1=Chris |last2=Bradsher |first2=Keith |date=4 March 2017 |title=Xi Jinping's Failed Promises Dim Hopes for Economic Change in 2nd Term |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/03/04/world/asia/china-xi-jinping-economic-reform.html |access-date=22 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref><ref name=\":30\" /> In 2015, the [[2015\u20132016 Chinese stock market turbulence|Chinese stock market bubble popped]], which led Xi to use state forces to fix the issue.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Wei |first=Lingling |date=10 December 2020 |title=China's Xi Ramps Up Control of Private Sector. 'We Have No Choice but to Follow the Party.' |language=en-US |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/china-xi-clampdown-private-sector-communist-party-11607612531 |access-date=22 August 2022 |issn=0099-9660}}</ref>\n\nXi has increased state control over China's economy, voicing support for China's state-owned enterprises (SOEs),<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.scmp.com/economy/china-economy/article/2166261/chinese-president-xi-jinpings-show-support-state-owned-firms|title=Chinese President Xi Jinping's show of support for state-owned firms 'no surprise', analysts say|last1=Wang|first1=Orange|date=28 September 2018|work=[[South China Morning Post]]|access-date=31 January 2020|last2=Leng|first2=Sidney}}</ref><ref name=\":30\" /> while also supporting the country's private sector.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.scmp.com/news/china/politics/article/2166108/xi-jinping-reassures-chinas-state-owned-enterprises-and-private|title=Xi says it's wrong to 'bad mouth' China's state firms... but country needs private sector as well|last=Gan|first=Nectar|date=28 September 2018|work=[[South China Morning Post]]|access-date=31 January 2020}}</ref> Under Xi, \"government guidance funds\", public-private investment funds set up by or for government bodies, have raised more than $900 billion for early funding to companies that work in sectors the government deems as strategic.<ref name=\":39\">{{Cite news |last=Lockett |first=Hudson |date=2022-06-12 |title=How Xi Jinping is reshaping China's capital markets |work=[[Financial Times]] |url=https://www.ft.com/content/d5b81ea0-5955-414c-b2eb-886dfed4dffe |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/hd68d |archive-date=11 December 2022 |url-access=subscription |url-status=live |access-date=2022-11-21}}</ref> Xi has increased the role of the [[Central Financial and Economic Affairs Commission]] at the expense of the [[State Council of the People's Republic of China|State Council]].<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.ft.com/content/57371736-4b69-11e6-88c5-db83e98a590a |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/5h5Wy |archive-date=11 December 2022 |url-access=subscription |url-status=live|title=Xi's China: The rise of party politics|last=Mitchell|first=Tom|date=25 July 2016|work=[[Financial Times]]|access-date=31 January 2020}}</ref> His administration made it easier for banks to issue [[Mortgage loan|mortgages]], increased foreign participation in the bond market, and increased the national currency [[Renminbi|renminbi's]] global role, helping it to join [[International Monetary Fund|IMF's]] basket of [[Special drawing rights|special drawing right]].<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/03/04/business/china-xi-jinping-economic-reform-scorecard.html |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170305071055/https://www.nytimes.com/2017/03/04/business/china-xi-jinping-economic-reform-scorecard.html |archive-date=5 March 2017 |url-access=limited |url-status=live|title=China and Economic Reform: Xi Jinping's Track Record|last=Bradsher|first=Keith|date=4 March 2017|work=[[The New York Times]]|access-date=31 January 2020|language=en-US|issn=0362-4331}}</ref> In the 40th anniversary of the launching of [[Chinese economic reform]]s in 2018, he has promised to continue reforms but has warned that nobody \"can dictate to the Chinese people\".<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.ft.com/content/658e78ce-0287-11e9-99df-6183d3002ee1 |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/e4iNT |archive-date=11 December 2022 |url-access=subscription |url-status=live|title=Xi says no one can 'dictate to the Chinese people'|last=Wildau|first=Gabriel|date=18 December 2018|work=[[Financial Times]]|access-date=31 January 2020}}</ref> Xi has also personally made eradicating extreme poverty through \"[[Targeted Poverty Alleviation|targeted poverty alleviation]]\" a key goal.<ref>{{Cite news |date=25 February 2021 |title=Xi Puts His Personal Stamp on China's Fight Against Poverty |language=en |work=Bloomberg News |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-02-25/china-s-xi-puts-personal-stamp-on-nation-s-fight-against-poverty |access-date=14 August 2022}}</ref> In 2021, Xi declared a \"complete victory\" over extreme poverty, saying that nearly 100 million people have been lifted out of poverty under his tenure, though some experts said that China's [[poverty threshold]] was relatively lower than the one set by the [[World Bank]].<ref>{{Cite news |date=25 February 2021 |title=China's Xi declares victory in ending extreme poverty |language=en-GB |work=[[BBC News]] |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-china-56194622 |access-date=14 August 2022}}</ref> In 2020, premier Li Keqiang, citing the [[National Bureau of Statistics of China|National Bureau of Statistics]] (NBS) said that China still had 600 million people living with less than 1000 yuan ($140) a month, although an article from ''[[The Economist]]'' said that the methodology NBS used was flawed, stating that the figure took the combined income, which was then equally divided.<ref>{{Cite news |date=18 June 2020 |title=China's poverty line is not as stingy as commentators think |newspaper=[[The Economist]] |location = Hong Kong|url=https://www.economist.com/finance-and-economics/2020/06/18/chinas-poverty-line-is-not-as-stingy-as-commentators-think |access-date=14 August 2022 |issn=0013-0613}}</ref>\n\nChina's economy has grown under Xi, with [[Gross domestic product|GDP in nominal terms]] more than doubling from $8.53 trillion in 2012 to $17.73 trillion in 2021,<ref>{{Cite web |title=GDP (current US$) \u2013 China {{!}} Data |url=https://data.worldbank.org/indicator/NY.GDP.MKTP.CD?locations=CN |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=[[World Bank]]}}</ref> though the rate of growth has slowed from 7.9% in 2012 to 6% in 2019.<ref>{{Cite web |title=GDP growth (annual %) \u2013 China {{!}} Data |url=https://data.worldbank.org/indicator/NY.GDP.MKTP.KD.ZG?locations=CN |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=[[World Bank]]}}</ref> Xi has stressed the importance of \"high-quality growth\" rather than \"inflated growth\".<ref>{{Cite web |last=Hui |first=Mary |date=16 February 2022 |title=What China means when it says it wants \"high quality\" GDP growth |url=https://qz.com/2119395/what-china-means-by-high-quality-economic-growth/ |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=[[Quartz (publication)|Quartz]] |language=en}}</ref> Xi has circulated a policy called \"[[dual circulation]]\", meaning reorienting the economy towards domestic consumption while remaining open to foreign trade and investment.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Wei |first=Lingling |date=12 August 2020 |title=China's Xi Speeds Up Inward Economic Shift |language=en-US |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/chinas-xi-speeds-up-inward-economic-shift-11597224602 |access-date=13 August 2022 |issn=0099-9660}}</ref> Xi has also made boosting [[productivity]] in the economy a priority.<ref>{{Cite news |date=14 August 2021 |title=China's future economic potential hinges on its productivity |newspaper=[[The Economist]] |url=https://www.economist.com/briefing/2021/08/14/chinas-future-economic-potential-hinges-on-its-productivity |access-date=13 August 2022 |issn=0013-0613}}</ref> Xi has attempted to reform the property sector to combat the steep increase in the property prices and to cut Chinese economy's dependence on the real estate sector.<ref>{{Cite news |date=27 July 2021 |title=China's Escalating Property Curbs Point to Xi's New Priority |language=en |work=Bloomberg News |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-07-27/china-s-escalating-property-curbs-underline-xi-s-new-priority |access-date=11 August 2022}}</ref> In the 19th CCP National Congress, Xi declared \"Houses are built to be inhabited, not for speculation\".<ref>{{Cite news |date=18 October 2017 |title=Housing Should Be for Living In, Not for Speculation, Xi Says |language=en |work=[[Bloomberg News]] |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2017-10-18/xi-renews-call-housing-should-be-for-living-in-not-speculation |access-date=11 August 2022}}</ref> In 2020, Xi's government formulated the \"[[three red lines]]\" policy that aimed to deleverage the heavily indebted property sector.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Lin |first1=Andy |last2=Hale |first2=Thomas |last3=Hudson |first3=Hudson |date=8 October 2021 |title=Half of China's top developers crossed Beijing's 'red lines' |work=[[Financial Times]] |url=https://www.ft.com/content/d5803d64-5cc5-46f0-bed0-1bc207440f9c |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/ouYkB |archive-date=11 December 2022 |url-access=subscription |url-status=live |access-date=11 August 2022}}</ref> Xi additionally has supported a [[property tax]], for which he has faced resistance from members of the CCP.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Wei |first=Lingling |date=19 October 2021 |title=In Tackling China's Real-Estate Bubble, Xi Jinping Faces Resistance to Property-Tax Plan |language=en-US |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/in-tackling-chinas-real-estate-bubble-xi-jinping-faces-resistance-to-property-tax-plan-11634650751 |access-date=11 August 2022 |issn=0099-9660}}</ref>\n\nXi's administration has promoted \"[[Made in China 2025]]\" plan that aims to make China self-reliant in key technologies, although publicly China de-emphasised this plan due to the outbreak of a [[China\u2013United States trade war|trade war]] with the U.S. Since the outbreak of the trade war in 2018, Xi has revived calls for \"self-reliance\", especially on the matters of technology.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Fifield |first=Anna |date=2 November 2018 |title=As China settles in for trade war, leader Xi emphasizes 'self reliance' |newspaper=[[The Washington Post]] |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/asia_pacific/as-china-settles-in-for-trade-war-leader-xi-emphasizesself-reliance/2018/11/01/2961b2b2-d8de-11e8-9559-712cbf726d1c_story.html |access-date=31 January 2020}}</ref> Xi's government has additionally allocated more than $100 billion to support China's efforts at [[semiconductor]] independence.<ref>{{Cite news |date=9 August 2022 |title=China Graft Probes Stem From Anger Over Failed Chip Plans |language=en |work=[[Bloomberg News]] |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2022-08-09/china-corruption-probes-stem-from-anger-over-failed-chip-plans |access-date=13 August 2022}}</ref> The Chinese government has also supported technology companies like [[Huawei]] through grants, tax breaks, credit facilities and other forms of assistance, enabling their rise but also leading to countermeasures by the U.S.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Yap |first=Chuin-Wei |date=25 December 2019 |title=State Support Helped Fuel Huawei's Global Rise |language=en-US |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/state-support-helped-fuel-huaweis-global-rise-11577280736 |access-date=16 September 2022 |issn=0099-9660}}</ref>\n\n{{Quote box\n| quote = Common prosperity is an essential requirement of socialism and a key feature of Chinese-style modernization. The common prosperity we are pursuing is for all, affluence both in material and spiritual life, but not for a small portion nor for uniform egalitarianism.\n| source = \u2014 Xi Jinping during a speech in 2021<ref name=\":35\" />\n| align = right\n| width = 25em\n}}\n\nIn November 2020, ''[[The Wall Street Journal]]'' reported that Xi personally ordered a halt to [[Ant Group]]'s [[initial public offering]] (IPO), in reaction to its founder [[Jack Ma]] criticizing government regulation in finance.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Wei |first=Jing Yang and Lingling |date=12 November 2020 |title=China's President Xi Jinping Personally Scuttled Jack Ma's Ant IPO |language=en-US |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/china-president-xi-jinping-halted-jack-ma-ant-ipo-11605203556 |access-date=11 August 2022 |issn=0099-9660}}</ref> Xi's administration has also overseen a decrease in offshore IPOs by Chinese companies, with most Chinese IPOs now taking place either in Shanghai or Shenzhen, and has increasingly directed funding to IPOs of companies that works in sectors it deems as strategic, including [[Electric vehicle|electric vehicles]], [[biotechnology]], [[renewable energy]], [[artificial intelligence]], semiconductors and other high-technology manufacturing.<ref name=\":39\" />\n\nSince 2021, Xi has promoted the term \"[[common prosperity]]\", a term which he defined as an \"essential requirement of socialism\",  described as affluence for all and said entailed reasonable adjustments to excess incomes.<ref name=\":35\">{{Cite web |date=19 October 2021 |title=Full Text: Xi Jinping's Speech on Boosting Common Prosperity \u2013 Caixin Global |url=https://www.caixinglobal.com/2021-10-19/full-text-xi-jinpings-speech-on-boosting-common-prosperity-101788302.html |access-date=11 August 2022 |website=[[Caixin Global]] |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |last=Hass |first=Ryan |date=9 September 2021 |title=Assessing China's \"common prosperity\" campaign |language=en-US |work=[[Brookings Institution]] |url=https://www.brookings.edu/blog/order-from-chaos/2021/09/09/assessing-chinas-common-prosperity-campaign/ |access-date=11 August 2022}}</ref> Common prosperity has been used as the justification for [[2020\u20132021 Xi Jinping Administration reform spree|large-scale crackdowns and regulations]] towards the perceived \"excesses\" of several sectors, most prominently tech and tutoring industries.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Shen |first1=Samuel |last2=Ranganathan |first2=Vidya |date=3 November 2021 |title=China stock pickers reshape portfolios on Xi's 'common prosperity' |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/technology/china-stock-pickers-reshape-portfolios-xis-common-prosperity-2021-11-02/ |access-date=11 August 2022}}</ref> The examples of actions taken against tech companies have included fining large tech companies<ref>{{cite news |last1=Moore |first1=Elena |date=10 April 2021 |title=China Fines Alibaba $2.8 Billion For Breaking Anti-Monopoly Law |language=en |publisher=[[NPR]] |url=https://www.npr.org/2021/04/10/986112628/china-fines-alibaba-2-8-billion-for-breaking-anti-monopoly-law |access-date=16 September 2021}}</ref> and passing of laws such as the [[Data Security Law of the People's Republic of China|Data Security Law]]. China also banned private tutoring companies from making profits and teaching school syllabus during weekends and holidays, effectively destroying the whole industry.<ref>{{Cite news |date=12 August 2021 |title=China's Education Crackdown Pushes Costly Tutors Underground |language=en |work=[[Bloomberg News]] |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-08-12/china-s-education-crackdown-pushes-costly-tutors-underground |access-date=13 August 2022}}</ref> Xi additionally opened a [[Beijing Stock Exchange|new stock exchange]] in Beijing targeted for small and medium enterprises (SMEs), which was another part of his common prosperity campaign.<ref>{{Cite news |last= |date=15 November 2021 |title=Trading kicks off on Beijing Stock Exchange, 10 stocks surge |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/china/trading-kicks-off-beijing-stock-exchange-10-stocks-surge-2021-11-15/ |access-date=22 August 2022}}</ref> There have also been other numerous cultural regulations, such as limiting video game usage by minors to 90 minutes during weekdays and 3 hours during weekends,<ref>{{Cite news |last=Buckley |first=Chris |date=30 August 2021 |title=China Tightens Limits for Young Online Gamers and Bans School Night Play |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2021/08/30/business/media/china-online-games.html |access-date=13 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> complete banning of [[cryptocurrency]],<ref>{{Cite news |last=Wallace |first=Elaine Yu and Joe |date=24 September 2021 |title=China Declares Cryptocurrency Transactions Illegal; Bitcoin Price Falls |language=en-US |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/china-declares-bitcoin-and-other-cryptocurrency-transactions-illegal-11632479288 |access-date=13 August 2022 |issn=0099-9660}}</ref> cracking down on idol worship, [[fandom]] and [[celebrity culture]]<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Stevenson |first1=Alexandra |last2=Chien |first2=Amy Chang |last3=Li |first3=Cao |date=27 August 2021 |title=China's Celebrity Culture Is Raucous. The Authorities Want to Change That. |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2021/08/27/business/media/china-celebrity-culture.html |access-date=13 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> and cracking down on \"[[Sissy|sissy men]]\".<ref>{{Cite web |last=McDonald |first=Joe |date=2 September 2021 |title=China bans 'sissy men' from TV in new cultural crackdown |url=https://www.latimes.com/world-nation/story/2021-09-02/china-bans-sissy-men-tv-new-crackdown-culture |access-date=17 September 2022 |website=[[Los Angeles Times]] |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\n===Reforms===\n====Agenda announcement====\nIn November 2013, at the conclusion of the Third Plenum of the 18th Central Committee, the Communist Party delivered a far-reaching reform agenda that alluded to changes in both economic and social policy. Xi signaled at the plenum that he was consolidating control of the massive internal security organization that was formerly the domain of [[Zhou Yongkang]].<ref name=\"brook2\">{{cite news |last1=Kroeber |first1=Arthur R. |date=17 November 2013 |title=Xi Jinping's Ambitious Agenda for Economic Reform in China |work=[[Brookings Institution]] |publisher= |url=http://www.brookings.edu/research/opinions/2013/11/17-xi-jinping-economic-agenda-kroeber |url-status=live |access-date=21 July 2014 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140727211348/http://www.brookings.edu/research/opinions/2013/11/17-xi-jinping-economic-agenda-kroeber |archive-date=27 July 2014}}</ref> A new National Security Commission was formed with Xi at its helm. The [[Central Leading Group for Comprehensively Deepening Reforms]]\u2014another ''ad hoc'' policy coordination body led by Xi upgraded to a commission in 2018\u2014was also formed to oversee the implementation of the reform agenda.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Jun |first=Mai |date=21 March 2018 |title=China unveils bold overhaul to tighten Communist Party control |url=https://www.scmp.com/news/china/policies-politics/article/2138291/china-unveils-bold-overhaul-tighten-communist-party |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=[[South China Morning Post]] |language=en}}</ref> Termed \"comprehensive deepening reforms\" ({{zh|labels=no|s=\u5168\u9762\u6df1\u5316\u6539\u9769|p=qu\u00e1nmi\u00e0n sh\u0113nhu\u00e0 g\u01ceig\u00e9}}), they were said to be the most significant since Deng Xiaoping's 1992 Southern Tour. The plenum also announced economic reforms and resolved to abolish the ''[[laogai]]'' system of \"[[Re-education through labor|re-education through labour]]\", which was largely seen as a blot on China's human rights record. The system has faced significant criticism for years from domestic critics and foreign observers.<ref name=\"brook2\" /> In January 2016, a [[two-child policy]] replaced the [[one-child policy]],<ref>{{cite news|last=Sridahan|first=Vasudevan|date=27 December 2015|title=China formally abolishes decades-old one-child policy|newspaper=[[International Business Times]]|url=http://www.ibtimes.co.uk/china-formally-abolishes-decades-old-one-child-policy-1535006|url-status=live|access-date=7 September 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190828224908/https://www.ibtimes.co.uk/china-formally-abolishes-decades-old-one-child-policy-1535006|archive-date=28 August 2019}}</ref> which was in turn was replaced with a [[three-child policy]] in May 2021.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Wee |first=Sui-Lee |date=31 May 2021 |title=China Says It Will Allow Couples to Have 3 Children, Up From 2 |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2021/05/31/world/asia/china-three-child-policy.html |access-date=11 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> In July 2021, all family size limits as well as penalties for exceeding them were removed.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Cheng |first=Evelyn |date=21 July 2021 |title=China scraps fines, will let families have as many children as they'd like |url=https://www.cnbc.com/2021/07/21/china-scraps-fines-for-families-violating-childbirth-limits.html |access-date=29 April 2022 |website=[[CNBC]] |language=en}}</ref>\n\n====Legal reforms====\nThe party under Xi announced a raft of [[Law reform|legal reforms]] at the Fourth Plenum held in the fall 2014, and he called for \"[[Rule of law in China|Chinese socialistic rule of law]]\" immediately afterwards. The party aimed to reform the legal system, which had been perceived as ineffective at delivering justice and affected by corruption, local government interference and lack of constitutional oversight. The plenum, while emphasizing the absolute leadership of the party, also called for a greater role of the constitution in the affairs of state and a strengthening of the role of the National People's Congress Standing Committee in interpreting the constitution.<ref name=\"scm32\">{{cite news|url=http://www.scmp.com/news/china/article/1623286/communist-party-pledges-greater-role-constitution-rights-fourth-plenum|title=Communist Party pledges greater role for constitution, rights in fourth plenum|last1=Zhou|first1=Laura|date=24 October 2014|work=[[South China Morning Post]]|access-date=7 September 2019|last2=Huang|first2=Cary|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181030035405/https://www.scmp.com/news/china/article/1623286/communist-party-pledges-greater-role-constitution-rights-fourth-plenum|archive-date=30 October 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> It also called for more transparency in legal proceedings, more involvement of ordinary citizens in the legislative process, and an overall \"professionalization\" of the legal workforce. The party also planned to institute cross-jurisdictional circuit legal tribunals as well as giving provinces consolidated administrative oversight over lower level legal resources, which is intended to reduce local government involvement in legal proceedings.<ref name=\"dww2\">{{cite news |last1=Doyon |first1=Jerome |last2=Winckler |first2=Hugo |date=20 November 2014 |title=The Fourth Plenum, Party Officials and Local Courts |work=[[Jamestown Foundation]] |publisher= |url=https://jamestown.org/program/the-fourth-plenum-party-officials-and-local-courts/ |access-date=7 September 2019}}</ref>\n\n====Military reforms====\n{{see also|Modernization of the People's Liberation Army|2015 People's Republic of China military reform|Military-civil fusion}}Since taking power in 2012, Xi has undertaken an overhaul of the [[People's Liberation Army]].<ref name=\":8\">{{Cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/investigates/special-report/china-army-xi/|title=How China is replacing America as Asia's military titan|last1=Lague|first1=David|date=23 April 2019|work=[[Reuters]]|access-date=10 January 2020|last2=Lim|first2=Benjamin Kang}}</ref> [[Military-civil fusion]] has advanced under Xi.<ref>{{Cite journal |last=Bitzinger |first=Richard A. |date=2021 |title=China's Shift from Civil-Military Integration to Military-Civil Fusion |url= |journal=Asia Policy |language=en |volume=28 |issue=1 |pages=5\u201324 |doi=10.1353/asp.2021.0001 |s2cid=234121234 |issn=1559-2960}}</ref><ref name=\"cnas\">{{cite journal |last1=B. Kania |first1=Elsa |last2=Laskai |first2=Lorand |date=28 January 2021 |title=Myths and Realities of China's Military-Civil Fusion Strategy |url=https://www.cnas.org/publications/reports/myths-and-realities-of-chinas-military-civil-fusion-strategy |website=[[Center for a New American Security]] |jstor=resrep28654 |jstor-access=free}}</ref> Xi has been active in his participation in military affairs, taking a direct hands-on approach to military reform. In addition to being the Chairman of the CMC and leader of the [[Central Leading Group for Military Reform]] founded in 2014 to oversee comprehensive military reforms, Xi has delivered numerous high-profile pronouncements vowing to clean up malfeasance and complacency in the military. Xi has repeatedly warned that the depoliticization of the PLA from the CCP would lead to a collapse similar to that of the Soviet Union.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Fifield |first=Anna |author-link=Anna Fifield |date=29 September 2019 |title=China's Communist Party has one more reason to celebrate \u2013 a year longer in power than the U.S.S.R. |newspaper=[[The Washington Post]] |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/asia_pacific/chinas-communist-party-has-one-more-reason-to-celebrate--a-year-longer-in-power-than-the-soviet-union/2019/09/28/993bb832-dfc0-11e9-be7f-4cc85017c36f_story.html |access-date=31 January 2020}}</ref> Xi held the New Gutian Conference in 2014, gathering China's top military officers, re-emphasizing the principle of \"the party has absolute control over the army\" first established by Mao at the 1929 [[Gutian Conference]].<ref name=\"meng2\">{{cite news|url=http://china.dwnews.com/news/2014-11-04/59616798.html|last1=Meng|first1=Chuan|date=4 November 2014|work=[[Duowei News]]|access-date=8 September 2019|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150121184703/http://china.dwnews.com/news/2014-11-04/59616798.html|archive-date=21 January 2015|language=zh-hans|script-title=zh:\u4e60\u8fd1\u5e73\u519b\u4e2d\"\u4eae\u5251\" \u65b0\u53e4\u7530\u4f1a\u8bae\u4e00\u7bad\u591a\u96d5|trans-title=Xi Jinping And Central Army's New \"Bright Sword\" Conference In Gutian Killed Many Birds With Only A Single Stone}}</ref>\n\n{{Quote box\n| quote = In the USSR, where the military was depoliticized, separated from the party and nationalized, the party was disarmed. When the Soviet Union came to crisis point, a big party was gone just like that. Proportionally, the Soviet Communist Party had more members than we do, but nobody was man enough to stand up and resist.\n| source = \u2014 Xi Jinping during a speech<ref name=\":12aa\">{{Cite news |last=Grammaticas |first=Damian |date=14 March 2013 |title=President Xi Jinping: A man with a dream |language=en-GB |work=[[BBC News]] |publisher= |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-china-21790384 |access-date=31 January 2020}}</ref>\n| align = right\n| width = 25em\n}}\n\nXi announced a reduction of 300,000 troops from the PLA in 2015, bringing its size to 2 million troops. Xi described this as a gesture of peace, while analysts such as Rory Medcalf have said that the cut was done to reduce costs as well as part of PLA's modernization.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/03/world/asia/beijing-turns-into-ghost-town-as-it-gears-up-for-military-parade.html |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150902221802/http://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/03/world/asia/beijing-turns-into-ghost-town-as-it-gears-up-for-military-parade.html |archive-date=2 September 2015 |url-access=limited |url-status=live|title=China Announces Cuts of 300,000 Troops at Military Parade Showing Its Might|last1=Wong|first1=Edward|date=2 September 2015|work=[[The New York Times]]|access-date=10 January 2020|last2=Perlez|first2=Jane|language=en-US|issn=0362-4331|last3=Buckley|first3=Chris}}</ref> On 2016, he reduced the number of [[Theater commands of the People's Liberation Army|theater commands of the PLA]] from seven to five.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://thediplomat.com/2016/02/its-official-chinas-military-has-5-new-theater-commands/|title=It's Official: China's Military Has 5 New Theater Commands|last=Tiezzi|first=Shannon|date=2 February 2016|work=[[The Diplomat]]|access-date=10 January 2020}}</ref> He has also abolished the four autonomous [[People's Liberation Army General Political Department|general departments]] of the PLA, replacing them with 15 agencies directly reporting to the CMC.<ref name=\":8\" /> Two new branches of the PLA were created under his reforms, the [[People's Liberation Army Strategic Support Force|Strategic Support Force]]<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://thediplomat.com/2017/02/chinas-strategic-support-force-a-force-for-innovation/|title=China's Strategic Support Force: A Force for Innovation?|last=Kania|first=Elsa|date=18 February 2017|work=[[The Diplomat]]|access-date=31 January 2020}}</ref> and the Joint Logistics Support Force.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Blanchard |first=Ben |date=14 September 2016 |title=China sets up new logistics force as part of military reforms |work=[[Reuters]] |publisher= |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-defence-idUSKCN11K05F |access-date=31 January 2020}}</ref>\n\nOn 21 April 2016, Xi was named [[Supreme Military Command of the People's Republic of China|commander-in-chief]] of the country's new Joint Operations Command Center of the PLA by [[Xinhua News Agency]] and the broadcaster [[China Central Television]].<ref name=\"Guardian21Apr162\">{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/apr/21/xi-jinping-named-commander-in-chief-chinese-state-media|title=Xi Jinping named as 'commander in chief' by Chinese state media|date=21 April 2016|work=[[The Guardian]]|access-date=25 April 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160425012825/http://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/apr/21/xi-jinping-named-commander-in-chief-chinese-state-media|archive-date=25 April 2016}}</ref><ref name=\"Independent21Apr162\">{{cite news|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/asia/chinese-president-xi-jinping-commander-in-chief-military-armed-forces-a6997396.html|title=Chinese President Xi Jinping named as military's 'commander-in-chief'|last1=Kayleigh|first1=Lewis|date=23 April 2016|work=[[The Independent]]|access-date=25 April 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160427091000/http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/asia/chinese-president-xi-jinping-commander-in-chief-military-armed-forces-a6997396.html|archive-date=27 April 2016}}</ref> Some analysts interpreted this move as an attempt to display strength and strong leadership and as being more \"political than military\".<ref name=\"ChinaTopix22Apr162\">{{cite news|url=http://www.chinatopix.com/articles/84000/20160422/president-xi-jinping-is-new-commander-in-chief-of-the-military.htm|title=President Xi Jinping is New Commander-in-Chief of the Military|last1=Sison|first1=Desiree|date=22 April 2016|work=China Topix|access-date=25 April 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160423120421/http://www.chinatopix.com/articles/84000/20160422/president-xi-jinping-is-new-commander-in-chief-of-the-military.htm|archive-date=23 April 2016}}</ref> According to Ni Lexiong, a military affairs expert, Xi \"not only controls the military but also does it in an absolute manner, and that in wartime, he is ready to command personally\".<ref name=\"ColuDaily24Apr20162\">{{cite news|url=http://www.columbiatribune.com/news/perspectives/china-s-xi-moves-to-take-more-direct-command-over/article_b5e96afb-97e6-533e-b33e-db5beab72bf3.html|title=China's Xi moves to take more direct command over military|date=24 April 2016|work=[[Columbia Daily Tribune]]|access-date=25 April 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160425105101/http://www.columbiatribune.com/news/perspectives/china-s-xi-moves-to-take-more-direct-command-over/article_b5e96afb-97e6-533e-b33e-db5beab72bf3.html|archive-date=25 April 2016}}</ref> According to a [[University of California, San Diego]] expert on Chinese military, Xi \"has been able to take political control of the military to an extent that exceeds what Mao and Deng have done\".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/10/11/world/asia/xi-jinping-military-china-purge.html|title=Xi Jinping Presses Military Overhaul, and Two Generals Disappear|last1=Buckley|first1=Chris|date=11 October 2017|newspaper=[[The New York Times]]|access-date=26 October 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171025083913/https://www.nytimes.com/2017/10/11/world/asia/xi-jinping-military-china-purge.html|archive-date=25 October 2017|last2=Myers|first2=Steven Lee}}</ref>\n\n===Foreign policy===\n{{main|Foreign policy of Xi Jinping}}\n[[File:President Biden met with President Xi of the PRC before the 2022 G20 Bali Summit.jpg|thumb|President Xi Jinping with President [[Joe Biden]] at the margins of the [[2022 G20 Bali summit]]]]\nXi has taken a harder line on security issues as well as foreign affairs, projecting a more nationalistic and assertive China on the world stage.<ref>{{Cite news |title=Xi Jinping has nurtured an ugly form of Chinese nationalism |newspaper=[[The Economist]] |url=https://www.economist.com/china/2022/07/13/xi-jinping-has-nurtured-an-ugly-form-of-chinese-nationalism |access-date=11 August 2022 |issn=0013-0613}}</ref> His political program calls for a China more united and confident of its own value system and political structure.<ref name=\"scmp32\">{{cite news|url=http://www.scmp.com/news/china/article/1586307/xi-jinping-rules-out-western-style-political-reform-china?page=all|title=Xi Jinping rules out Western-style political reform for China|last1=Meng|first1=Angela|date=6 September 2014|work=[[South China Morning Post]]|access-date=7 September 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180818085415/https://www.scmp.com/news/china/article/1586307/xi-jinping-rules-out-western-style-political-reform-china?page=all|archive-date=18 August 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> Foreign analysts and observers have frequently said that Xi's main foreign policy objective is to restore China's position on the global stage as a [[great power]].<ref>{{Cite news |last=Buckley |first=Chris |date=26 February 2018 |title=Xi Jinping Thought Explained: A New Ideology for a New Era |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2018/02/26/world/asia/xi-jinping-thought-explained-a-new-ideology-for-a-new-era.html |access-date=21 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref><ref name=\":12aa\"/><ref>{{Cite journal |last1=Barrass |first1=Gordon |last2=Inkster |first2=Nigel |date=2 January 2018 |title=Xi Jinping: The Strategist Behind the Dream |url=https://doi.org/10.1080/00396338.2018.1427363 |journal=Survival |volume=60 |issue=1 |pages=41\u201368 |doi=10.1080/00396338.2018.1427363 |s2cid=158856300 |issn=0039-6338}}</ref>\n\nAddressing a [[Conference on Interaction and Confidence-Building Measures in Asia|regional conference]] in Shanghai on 21 May 2014, he called on Asian countries to unite and forge a way together, rather than get involved with third party powers, seen as a reference to the United States. \"Matters in Asia ultimately must be taken care of by Asians. Asia's problems ultimately must be resolved by Asians and Asia's security ultimately must be protected by Asians\", he told the conference.<ref name=\"TerritorialDisputes2\">{{cite news |date=21 May 2014 |title=Asian nations should avoid military ties with third party powers, says China's Xi |newspaper=China National News |url=http://www.chinanationalnews.com/index.php/sid/222207019/scat/9366300fc9319e9b/ht/Asian-nations-should-avoid-military-ties-with-third-party-powers-says-Chinas-Xi |access-date=21 May 2014 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140522071827/http://www.chinanationalnews.com/index.php/sid/222207019/scat/9366300fc9319e9b/ht/Asian-nations-should-avoid-military-ties-with-third-party-powers-says-Chinas-Xi |archive-date=22 May 2014}}</ref>\n\nXi has promoted \"major-country diplomacy\" ({{zh|s=\u5927\u56fd\u5916\u4ea4|labels=no}}), stating that China is already a \"big power\" and breaking away from previous Chinese leaders who had a more precautious diplomacy.<ref>{{Cite journal |last=Hu |first=Weixing |date=2 January 2019 |title=Xi Jinping's 'Major Country Diplomacy': The Role of Leadership in Foreign Policy Transformation |url=https://doi.org/10.1080/10670564.2018.1497904 |journal=Journal of Contemporary China |volume=28 |issue=115 |pages=1\u201314 |doi=10.1080/10670564.2018.1497904 |s2cid=158345991 |issn=1067-0564}}</ref> He has adopted a hawkish foreign policy posture called \"[[wolf warrior diplomacy]]\",<ref>{{Cite web |last=Auto |first=Hermes |date=5 April 2021 |title=China's 'wolf warrior' diplomats back to howl at Xinjiang critics |url=https://www.straitstimes.com/asia/east-asia/chinas-wolf-warrior-diplomats-back-to-howl-at-xinjiang-critics |access-date=11 August 2022 |website=[[The Straits Times]] |language=en}}</ref> while his foreign policy thoughts are collectively known as \"[[Xi Jinping Thought on Diplomacy]]\".<ref>{{Cite web |last=Bishop |first=Bill |date=8 March 2019 |title=Xi's thought on diplomacy is \"epoch-making\" |url=https://www.axios.com/2019/03/08/xis-diplomacy-epoch-making |access-date=11 August 2022 |website=[[Axios (website)|Axios]] |language=en}}</ref> In March 2021, he said that \"the East is rising and the West is declining\" ({{zh|s=\u4e1c\u5347\u897f\u964d|labels=no}}), saying that the power of the [[Western world]] was in decline and their COVID-19 response was an example of this, and that China was entering a period of opportunity because of this.<ref name=\":2\">{{Cite news |last=Buckley |first=Chris |date=3 March 2021 |title='The East Is Rising': Xi Maps Out China's Post-Covid Ascent |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/03/world/asia/xi-china-congress.html |access-date=12 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> In 2022, Xi proposed a \"[[Global Security Initiative|global security initiative]]\" that upheld the term \"[[indivisible security]]\", a term also supported by Russia.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Yao |first1=Kevin |last2=Tian |first2=Yew Lun |date=22 April 2022 |title=China's Xi proposes 'global security initiative', without giving details |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/china/chinas-xi-says-unilateral-sanctions-will-not-work-2022-04-21/ |access-date=13 August 2022}}</ref> Xi has frequently alluded to \"[[Community of Common Destiny|community with a shared future for mankind]]\", which Chinese diplomats have said doesn't imply an intention to change the international order,<ref name=\"Zhang\">{{cite journal |last=Zhang |first=Denghua |date=May 2018 |title=The Concept of 'Community of Common Destiny' in China's Diplomacy: Meaning, Motives and Implications |journal=Asia & the Pacific Policy Studies |volume=5 |issue=2 |pages=196\u2013207 |doi=10.1002/app5.231 |doi-access=free}}</ref> but which foreign observers say China wants a new order that puts it more at the centre.<ref>{{Cite journal |last=Tobin |first=Liza |date=2018 |others=The University Of Texas At Austin, The University Of Texas At Austin |title=Xi's Vision for Transforming Global Governance: A Strategic Challenge for Washington and Its Allies (November 2018) |url=https://tnsr.org/2018/11/xis-vision-for-transforming-global-governance-a-strategic-challenge-for-washington-and-its-allies/ |journal=Texas National Security Review |language=en |doi=10.26153/TSW/863 |doi-access=free}}</ref> Under Xi, China has, along with Russia, also focused on increasing relations with the [[Global North and Global South|Global South]] in order to blunt the effect of Western sanctions.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Seib |first=Gerald F. |date=15 July 2022 |title=Putin and Xi's Bet on the Global South |language=en-US |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/putin-and-xis-bet-on-the-global-south-11657897521 |access-date=21 August 2022 |issn=0099-9660}}</ref>\n\nXi has put an emphasis on increasing China's \"international discourse power\" ({{zh|s=\u56fd\u9645\u8bdd\u8bed\u6743|labels=no}}) to create a more favorable global opinion of China in the world.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Jones |first=Hugo |date=24 November 2021 |title=China's Quest for Greater 'Discourse Power' |url=https://thediplomat.com/2021/11/chinas-quest-for-greater-discourse-power/ |access-date=29 August 2022 |website=[[The Diplomat]] |language=en-US}}</ref> In this pursuit, Xi has emphasised the need to \"tell China's story well\" ({{zh|s=\u8bb2\u597d\u4e2d\u56fd\u6545\u4e8b|labels=no}}), meaning expanding China's external propaganda ({{zh|s=\u5916\u5ba3|labels=no}}) and communications.<ref>{{Cite web |date=16 April 2021 |title=Telling China's Story Well |url=https://chinamediaproject.org/the_ccp_dictionary/telling-chinas-story-well/ |access-date=29 August 2022 |website=China Media Project |language=en-US}}</ref> Xi has expanded the focus and scope of the [[United Front (China)|United Front]], which aims to consolidate support for CCP in non-CCP elements both inside and outside China, and has accordingly expanded the [[United Front Work Department]].<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Kynge |first1=James |author-link=James Kynge |last2=Hornby |first2=Lucy |last3=Anderlini |first3=Jamil |date=26 October 2017 |title=Inside China's secret 'magic weapon' for worldwide influence |work=[[Financial Times]] |url=https://www.ft.com/content/fb2b3934-b004-11e7-beba-5521c713abf4 |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/W1lM5 |archive-date=11 December 2022 |url-access=subscription |url-status=live |access-date=21 August 2022}}</ref>\n\n====Africa====\n{{Main articles|Sino-African relations}}\n\nUnder Xi, China has cut back lending to Africa after fears that African countries couldn't repay their debts to China.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Hille |first1=Kathrin |last2=Pilling |first2=David |date=11 January 2022 |title=China applies brakes to Africa lending |work=[[Financial Times]] |url=https://www.ft.com/content/64b4bcd5-032e-4be5-aa3b-e902f5b1345e |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/20221211/https://www.ft.com/content/64b4bcd5-032e-4be5-aa3b-e902f5b1345e |archive-date=11 December 2022 |url-access=subscription |url-status=live |access-date=21 August 2022}}</ref> Xi has also promised that China would write off debts of some African countries.<ref>{{Cite web |last=He |first=Laura |title=China is promising to write off some loans to Africa. It may just be a drop in the ocean |url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/06/19/economy/china-xi-jinping-africa-intl-hnk/index.html |access-date=21 August 2022 |website=[[CNN]]|date=19 June 2020 }}</ref> In November 2021, Xi promised African nations 1 billion doses of China's COVID-19 vaccines, which was in addition to the 200 million already supplied before. This has been said to be part of China's [[vaccine diplomacy]].<ref>{{Cite web |date=29 November 2021 |title=China's Xi promises 1bn COVID-19 vaccine doses to Africa |url=https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/11/29/chinas-xi-promises-1-billion-covid-19-vaccine-doses-to-africa |access-date=21 August 2022 |website=[[Al Jazeera]] |language=en}}</ref>\n\n====European Union====\n{{Main|China\u2013European Union relations}}\n\nChina's efforts under Xi has been for the European Union (EU) to stay in a neutral position in their contest with the U.S.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Buckley |first1=Chris |last2=Bradsher |first2=Keith |date=15 April 2022 |title=Faced With a Changed Europe, China Sticks to an Old Script |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2022/04/15/world/asia/china-europe-russia-ukraine.html |access-date=13 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> China and the EU announced the [[Comprehensive Agreement on Investment]] (CAI) in 2020, although the deal was later frozen due to mutual sanctions over Xinjiang.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Miller |first=Michael E. |title=China says Macron and Merkel support reviving E.U.-China investment pact. Not so fast. |language=en-US |newspaper=[[The Washington Post]] |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2021/07/06/china-europe-investment-uyghurs/ |access-date=13 August 2022 |issn=0190-8286}}</ref> Xi has supported calls for EU to achieve \"[[strategic autonomy]]\",<ref>{{Cite web |last=Wang |first=Amber |date=14 December 2021 |title=Dangers for China in the EU drive for strategic autonomy: analyst |url=https://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy/article/3159657/dangers-china-eu-drive-strategic-autonomy-analyst |access-date=12 August 2022 |website=[[South China Morning Post]] |language=en}}</ref> and has also called on the EU to view China \"independently\".<ref>{{Cite news |last= |date=1 April 2022 |title=China's Xi calls on EU to view China 'independently' -state media |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/china/chinas-xi-calls-eu-view-china-independently-state-media-2022-04-01/ |access-date=13 August 2022}}</ref>\n\n====India====\n{{Main|China\u2013India relations}}Relations between China and India had ups and downs under Xi, later deteriorating due to various factors. In 2013, the two countries had a [[2013 Depsang standoff|standoff in Depsang]] for three weeks, which ended with no border change.<ref>{{Cite news |date=6 May 2013 |title=India says China agrees retreat to de facto border in faceoff deal |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-india-china-idUSBRE9440B220130506 |access-date=29 August 2022}}</ref> In 2017, the two countries [[2017 China\u2013India border standoff|again had a standoff]] over a Chinese construction of a road in [[Doklam]], a territory both claimed by [[Bhutan]], India's ally, and China,<ref>{{Cite news |date=3 July 2017 |title=China says India violates 1890 agreement in border stand-off |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-india-idUSKBN19O109 |access-date=29 August 2022}}</ref> though by 28 August, both countries mutually disengaged.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Gettleman |first1=Jeffrey |last2=Hern\u00e1ndez |first2=Javier C. |date=28 August 2017 |title=China and India Agree to Ease Tensions in Border Dispute |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/08/28/world/asia/china-india-standoff-withdrawal.html |access-date=29 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> The most serious crisis in the relationship came when the two countries had a [[2020\u20132022 China\u2013India skirmishes|deadly clash in 2020]] at the [[Line of Actual Control]], leaving some soldiers dead.<ref>{{cite news |last=Janjua |first=Haroon |date=10 May 2020 |title=Chinese and Indian troops injured in border brawl |newspaper=[[The Times]] |url=https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/chinese-and-indian-troops-injured-in-border-brawl-3gsfwp37r |url-status=live |access-date=12 May 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200512042352/https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/chinese-and-indian-troops-injured-in-border-brawl-3gsfwp37r |archive-date=12 May 2020 |issn=0140-0460}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last=France-Presse |first=Agence |date=11 May 2020 |title=Indian and Chinese soldiers injured in cross-border fistfight, says Delhi |work=[[The Guardian]] |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/may/11/indian-and-chinese-soldiers-injured-in-cross-border-fistfight-says-delhi |url-status=live |access-date=12 May 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200512035152/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/may/11/indian-and-chinese-soldiers-injured-in-cross-border-fistfight-says-delhi |archive-date=12 May 2020 |issn=0261-3077}}</ref> The clashes created a serious deterioration in relations, with China seizing a small chunk of territory that India controlled.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Myers |first1=Steven Lee |last2=Abi-Habib |first2=Maria |last3=Gettleman |first3=Jeffrey |date=17 June 2020 |title=In China-India Clash, Two Nationalist Leaders With Little Room to Give |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/06/17/world/asia/china-india-border.html |access-date=29 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref>\n\n====Japan====\n{{Main|China\u2013Japan relations}}\nChina\u2013Japan relations have initially soured under Xi's administration; the most thorny issue between the two countries remains the dispute over the [[Senkaku islands]], which China calls Diaoyu. In response to Japan's continued robust stance on the issue, China declared an [[Air Defense Identification Zone (East China Sea)|Air Defense Identification Zone]] in November 2013.<ref name=\"osawa2\">{{cite news |last1=Osawa |first1=Jun |date=17 December 2013 |title=China's ADIZ over the East China Sea: A \"Great Wall in the Sky\"? |publisher=[[Brookings Institution]] |url=http://www.brookings.edu/research/opinions/2013/12/17-china-air-defense-identification-zone-osawa |url-status=live |access-date=7 September 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160714181744/http://www.brookings.edu/research/opinions/2013/12/17-china-air-defense-identification-zone-osawa |archive-date=14 July 2016}}</ref> However, the relations later started to improve, with Xi being invited to visit in 2020,<ref>{{Cite web |last=Albert |first=Eleanor |date=16 March 2019 |title=China and Japan's Rapprochement Continues \u2013 For Now |url=https://thediplomat.com/2019/05/china-and-japans-rapprochement-continues-for-now/ |access-date=12 August 2022 |website=The Diplomat |language=en-US}}</ref> though the trip was later delayed due to the COVID-19 pandemic.<ref>{{Cite news |date=28 February 2021 |title=China's Xi will not make a state visit to Japan this year -Sankei |language=en |work=Reuters |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/uk-japan-china-xi-idUKKCN2AS0SU |access-date=12 August 2022}}</ref> In August 2022, [[Kyodo News]] reported that Xi personally decided to let ballistic missiles to land within Japan's exclusive economic zone (EEZ) during the [[2022 Chinese military exercises around Taiwan|military exercises held around Taiwan]], to send a warning to Japan.<ref>{{Cite web |last= |first= |date=11 August 2022 |title=Xi let missiles fall in Japan EEZ during Taiwan drills: sources |url=https://english.kyodonews.net/news/2022/08/2e93a85c08b8-urgent-xi-decided-to-let-missiles-fall-in-japan-eez-during-taiwan-drills.html |access-date=12 August 2022 |website=[[Kyodo News]]}}</ref>\n\n====Taiwan====\n{{Further|Cross-Strait relations|Ma\u2013Xi meeting}}\n[[File:2015 Ma\u2013Xi Meeting 08.jpg|thumb|Xi Jinping met with then-Taiwanese president [[Ma Ying-jeou]] in November 2015 in their capacity as the leader of mainland China and Taiwan respectively.]]\n\nIn 2015, Xi met with Taiwanese president [[Ma Ying-jeou]], which marked the first time the political leaders of both sides of the [[Taiwan Strait]] have met since the end of the [[Chinese Civil War]] in Mainland China in 1950.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/11/04/world/asia/leaders-of-china-and-taiwan-to-meet-for-first-time-since-1949.html|title=China, Taiwan and a Meeting After 66 Years|last1=Perlez|first1=Jane|date=4 November 2015|work=[[The New York Times]]|access-date=1 November 2017|last2=Ramzy|first2=Austin|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170903072421/https://www.nytimes.com/2015/11/04/world/asia/leaders-of-china-and-taiwan-to-meet-for-first-time-since-1949.html|archive-date=3 September 2017|url-status=live}}</ref> Xi said that China and Taiwan are \"[[Zhonghua minzu|one family]]\" that cannot be pulled apart.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.straitstimes.com/singapore/one-minute-handshake-marks-historic-meeting-between-xi-jinping-and-ma-ying-jeou|title=One-minute handshake marks historic meeting between Xi Jinping and Ma Ying-jeou|date=7 November 2015|work=[[The Straits Times]]|access-date=5 September 2019|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190905182113/https://www.straitstimes.com/singapore/one-minute-handshake-marks-historic-meeting-between-xi-jinping-and-ma-ying-jeou|archive-date=5 September 2019}}</ref> However, the relations started deteriorating after [[Tsai Ing-wen]] of the [[Democratic Progressive Party]] (DPP) won the [[2016 Taiwanese presidential election|presidential elections in 2016]].<ref>{{Cite web |last=Huang |first=Kristin |date=15 June 2021 |title=Timeline: Taiwan's relations with mainland China under Tsai Ing-wen |url=https://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy/article/3137231/timeline-cross-strait-relations-under-taiwans-president-tsai |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=[[South China Morning Post]] |language=en}}</ref>\n\nIn the 19th Party Congress held in 2017, Xi reaffirmed six of the nine principles that had been affirmed continuously since the 16th Party Congress in 2002, with the notable exception of \"Placing hopes on the [[People of Taiwan|Taiwan people]] as a force to help bring about [[Chinese unification|unification]]\".<ref name=\"Brookings R.C. Bush2\">{{Cite news|url=https://www.brookings.edu/blog/order-from-chaos/2017/10/19/what-xi-jinping-said-about-taiwan-at-the-19th-party-congress/|title=What Xi Jinping said about Taiwan at the 19th Party Congress|last=Bush|first=Richard C.|date=19 October 2017|publisher=[[Brookings Institution]]|access-date=8 July 2018|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180708013012/https://www.brookings.edu/blog/order-from-chaos/2017/10/19/what-xi-jinping-said-about-taiwan-at-the-19th-party-congress/|archive-date=8 July 2018}}</ref> According to the [[Brookings Institution]], Xi used stronger language on potential [[Taiwan independence movement|Taiwan independence]] than his predecessors towards previous DPP governments in Taiwan.<ref name=\"Brookings R.C. Bush2\" /> He said that \"we will never allow any person, any organisation, or any political party to split any part of the Chinese territory from China at any time at any form.\"<ref name=\"Brookings R.C. Bush2\" /> In March 2018, Xi said that Taiwan would face the \"punishment of history\" for any attempts at separatism.<ref name=\":22\">{{Cite news|url=https://www.afr.com/news/politics/world/xi-jinping-warns-taiwan-it-will-face-punishment-of-history-for-separatism-20180320-h0xpx4|title=Xi Jinping warns Taiwan it will face 'punishment of history' for separatism|last1=Wen|first1=Philip|date=20 March 2018|work=[[The Australian Financial Review]]|access-date=8 July 2018|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180708192153/https://www.afr.com/news/politics/world/xi-jinping-warns-taiwan-it-will-face-punishment-of-history-for-separatism-20180320-h0xpx4|archive-date=8 July 2018|last2=Qiu|first2=Stella|url-access=subscription}}</ref>\n\nIn January 2019, Xi Jinping called on Taiwan to reject its formal independence from China, saying: \"We make no promise to renounce the use of force and reserve the option of taking all necessary means.\" Those options, he said, could be used against \"external interference\". Xi also said that they \"are willing to create broad space for peaceful reunification, but will leave no room for any form of separatist activities.\"<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2019/jan/02/all-necessary-means-xi-jinping-reserves-right-to-use-force-against-taiwan|title='All necessary means': Xi Jinping reserves right to use force against Taiwan|last=Kuo|first=Lily|date=2 January 2019|work=[[The Guardian]]|access-date=7 September 2019|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190822114526/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2019/jan/02/all-necessary-means-xi-jinping-reserves-right-to-use-force-against-taiwan|archive-date=22 August 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last=Griffiths |first=James |date=2 January 2019 |title=Xi warns Taiwan independence is 'a dead end' |work=[[CNN]] |publisher= |url=https://edition.cnn.com/2019/01/02/asia/xi-jinping-taiwan-tsai-intl/ |url-status=live |access-date=7 September 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191003215248/https://edition.cnn.com/2019/01/02/asia/xi-jinping-taiwan-tsai-intl/ |archive-date=3 October 2019}}</ref> President Tsai responded to the speech by saying Taiwan would not accept a [[one country, two systems]] arrangement with the mainland, while stressing the need for all cross-strait negotiations to be on a government-to-government basis.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-taiwan-president/taiwan-president-defiant-after-china-calls-for-reunification-idUSKCN1OW0FN|title=Taiwan president defiant after China calls for reunification|last=Lee|first=Yimou|date=2 January 2019|publisher=[[Reuters]]|access-date=7 September 2019|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190929044514/https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-taiwan-president/taiwan-president-defiant-after-china-calls-for-reunification-idUSKCN1OW0FN|archive-date=29 September 2019}}</ref>\n\nIn 2022, after the Chinese military exercises around Taiwan, the PRC published a white paper called \"[[The Taiwan Question and China\u2019s Reunification in the New Era]]\", which was the first white paper regards to Taiwan since 2000.<ref name=\":13\">{{Cite news |last=Millson |first=Alex |date=10 August 2022 |title=China's First White Paper on Taiwan Since Xi Came to Power \u2014 In Full |language=en |work=[[Bloomberg News]] |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2022-08-10/china-s-first-white-paper-on-taiwan-since-xi-came-to-power-in-full |access-date=12 August 2022}}</ref> The paper urged Taiwan to become a [[Special administrative regions of China|special administrative region]] of the PRC under the one country two systems formula,<ref name=\":13\" /> and said that \"a small number of countries, the U.S. foremost amongst them\" are \"using Taiwan to contain China\".<ref name=\":14\">{{Cite web |last=Falconer |first=Rebecca |date=11 August 2022 |title=New Beijing policy removes pledge not to send troops to Taiwan if it takes control of island |url=https://www.axios.com/2022/08/11/beijing-taiwan-policy-update-troops-pledge |access-date=12 August 2022 |website=[[Axios (website)|Axios]] |language=en}}</ref> Notably, the new white paper excluded a part that previously said the PRC would not send troops or officials to Taiwan after unification.<ref name=\":14\" />\n\n====Middle East====\n[[File:Ali Khamenei met with Xi Jinping in Tehran 2016 (1).jpg|thumb|Xi with Iran's supreme leader [[Ali Khamenei]], 23 January 2016]]\n\nWhile China has historically been wary of getting closer to the [[Middle East]] countries, Xi has changed this approach.<ref name=\":31\">{{Cite web |last=Vohra |first=Anchal |date=1 February 2022 |title=Xi Jinping Has Transformed China's Middle East Policy |url=https://foreignpolicy.com/2022/02/01/xi-jinping-has-transformed-chinas-middle-east-policy/ |access-date=8 September 2022 |website=[[Foreign Policy]] |language=en-US}}</ref> China has grown closer to both Iran and Saudi Arabia under Xi.<ref name=\":31\" /> During a visit to Iran in 2016, Xi proposed a [[Iran\u2013China 25-year Cooperation Program|large cooperation program]] with Iran,<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Fassihi |first1=Farnaz |last2=Myers |first2=Steven Lee |date=11 July 2020 |title=Defying U.S., China and Iran Near Trade and Military Partnership |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/07/11/world/asia/china-iran-trade-military-deal.html |access-date=14 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> a deal that was later signed in 2021.<ref>{{Cite news |date=27 March 2021 |title=Iran and China sign 25-year cooperation agreement |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-iran-china-idUSKBN2BJ0AD |access-date=14 August 2022}}</ref> China has also sold ballistic missiles to Saudi Arabia and is helping build 7,000 schools in Iraq.<ref name=\":31\" /> In 2013, Xi proposed a peace deal between Israel and Palestine that entails a [[two-state solution]] based on the [[Green Line (Israel)|1967 borders]].<ref>{{Cite web |last2=Alemdaroglu |first2=Ayca |date=16 September 2020 |title=Erdogan Is Turning Turkey Into a Chinese Client State |url=https://foreignpolicy.com/2020/09/16/erdogan-is-turning-turkey-into-a-chinese-client-state/ |access-date=8 September 2022 |website=[[Foreign Policy]] |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\n====North Korea====\n{{Main|China\u2013North Korea relations}}\nUnder Xi, China has initially taken a more critical stance on North Korea due to [[North Korea and weapons of mass destruction|its nuclear tests]].<ref name=\"chengli2\">{{cite news |last1=Li |first1=Cheng |date=26 September 2014 |title=A New Type of Major Power Relationship? |publisher=[[Brookings Institution]] |last3=Zheng |first3=Sarah |date=27 March 2018 |title=Kim's visit evidence China, North Korea remain allies, analysts say |language=en |newspaper=[[South China Morning Post]] |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190725192608/https://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy-defence/article/2139178/rumours-china-and-north-korea-were-no-longer-allies-put |archive-date=25 July 2019}}</ref> Xi has also supported denuclearization of North Korea,<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Song |first1=Jung-a |last2=Shepherd |first2=Christian |date=21 June 2019 |title=Xi Jinping vows active role |first=Christopher |date=20 April 2021 |title=China's Xi pushes economic reform at North Korea summit |url=https://apnews.com/article/weapons-programs-ap-top-news-north-korea-international-news-nuclear-weapons-8d5f00b17403495db198e993aeb1c73c |access-date=14 August 2022 |website=Associated Press |language=en}}</ref> At the [[2019 G20 Osaka summit|G20 meeting in Japan]], Xi called for a \"timely easing\" of [[Sanctions against North Korea|sanctions imposed on North Korea]].<ref>{{Cite news |last=Lee |first=Jeong-ho |date=2 July 2019 |title=Xi calls for 'timely' easing of North Korea sanctions after Trump-Kim meeting |language=en |newspaper=[[South China Morning Post]]
