|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190823115523/https://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy/article/3016981/beijing-reaffirms-support-gradual-easing-north-korea-sanctions |archive-date=23 August 2019}}</ref>\n\n====Russia====\n{{Main|China\u2013Russia relations}}\n[[File:\u041f\u0430\u0440\u0430\u0434 \u0432 \u0447\u0435\u0441\u0442\u044c 70-\u043b\u0435\u0442\u0438\u044f \u0412\u0435\u043b\u0438\u043a\u043e\u0439 \u041f\u043e\u0431\u0435\u0434\u044b - 26.jpg|thumb|Xi with the first lady during the [[2015 Moscow Victory Day Parade|Moscow Victory Day Parade on 9 May 2015]]]]\n\nXi has cultivated [[China\u2013Russia relations|stronger relations with Russia]], particularly in the wake of the [[2014 pro-Russian unrest in Ukraine|Ukraine crisis]] of 2014. He seems to have developed a strong personal relationship with president Vladimir Putin. Both are viewed as strong leaders with a nationalist orientation who are not afraid to assert themselves against Western interests.<ref name=\"russia22\">{{cite news |last1=Baker |first1=Peter |date=8 November 2014 |title=As Russia Draws Closer to China, U.S. Faces a New Challenge |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2014/11/09/world/vladimir-putin-xi-jinping-form-closer-ties.html |url-status=live |access-date=7 September 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190828224309/https://www.nytimes.com/2014/11/09/world/vladimir-putin-xi-jinping-form-closer-ties.html |archive-date=28 August 2019}}</ref> Xi attended the opening ceremonies of the 2014 Winter Olympics in Sochi. Under Xi, China signed a $400&nbsp;billion [[Natural gas in Russia|gas deal with Russia]]; China has also become Russia's largest trading partner.<ref name=\"russia22\" />\n\nXi and Putin met on 4 February 2022 during the run up to the [[2022 Winter Olympics|2022 Beijing Olympics]] during the massive Russian [[Prelude to the 2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine|build-up of force]] on the Ukrainian border, with the two expressing that the two countries are nearly united in their [[Anti-Americanism|anti-US alignment]] and that both nations shared \"no limits\" to their commitments.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Mauldin |first=Chao Deng, Ann M. Simmons, Evan Gershkovich and William |date=4 February 2022 |title=Putin, Xi Aim Russia-China Partnership Against U.S. |language=en-US |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/russias-vladimir-putin-meets-with-chinese-leader-xi-jinping-in-beijing-11643966743 |issn=0099-9660}}</ref><ref name=\"Xi-Putin\">{{Cite news |last1=Buckley |first1=Chris |last2=Myers |first2=Steven Lee |date=7 March 2022 |title='No Wavering': After Turning to Putin, Xi Faces Hard Wartime Choices for China |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2022/03/07/world/asia/putin-ukraine-china-xi.html |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> U.S. officials said that China had asked Russia to wait for the [[2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine|invasion of Ukraine]] until after the Beijing Olympics ended on 20 February.<ref name=\"Xi-Putin\" /> In April 2022, Xi Jinping expressed opposition to [[International sanctions during the Russo-Ukrainian War|sanctions against Russia]].<ref>{{cite news |last=Ng |first=Teddy |date=2 April 2022 |title=Chinese President Xi Jinping warns it could take decades to repair economic damage caused by Ukraine crisis |work=[[South China Morning Post]] |url=https://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy/article/3172860/chinese-president-xi-jinping-warns-it-could-take-decades |access-date=12 August 2022}}</ref> On 15 June 2022, Xi Jinping reasserted China's [[China and the 2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine|support for Russia]] on issues of sovereignty and security.<ref>{{cite news |last=Lau |first=Stuart |date=15 June 2022 |title=China's Xi gives most direct backing to Putin since invasion |work=[[Politico]] |url=https://www.politico.eu/article/china-xi-give-most-direct-backing-putin-invasion-ukraine/ |access-date=12 August 2022}}</ref> However, Xi also said China is committed to respecting \"the territorial integrity of all countries\",<ref>{{Cite web |title=China's Xi Says International Disputes Should be Resolved Via Dialogue, Not Sanctions |url=https://www.voanews.com/a/china-s-xi-says-international-disputes-should-be-resolved-via-dialogue-not-sanctions/6538799.html |access-date=12 August 2022 |website=[[Voice of America]] |language=en}}</ref> and said China was \"pained to see the flames of war reignited in Europe\".<ref>{{Cite web |date=9 March 2022 |title=China's Xi: Beijing supports peace talks between Russia, Ukraine |url=https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2022/3/9/chinas-xi-beijing-supports-peace-talks-between-russia-ukraine |access-date=12 August 2022 |website=[[Al Jazeera]] |language=en}}</ref> China has additionally kept a distance from Russia's actions, instead putting itself as a neutral party.<ref name=\"Xi-Putin\" />\n\nDuring the war Ukrainian president [[Volodymyr Zelenskyy]] has given a nuanced take to China,<ref>{{Cite news |last=Santora |first=Marc |date=2022-08-03 |title=On China, the normally forceful Zelensky offers a nuanced view. |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2022/08/03/world/europe/on-china-the-normally-forceful-zelensky-offers-a-nuanced-view.html |access-date=2022-10-26 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> saying that the country has the economic leverage to pressure Putin to end the war, adding \"I\u2019m sure that without the Chinese market for the Russian Federation, Russia would be feeling complete economic isolation. That\u2019s something that China can do \u2013 to limit the trade [with Russia] until the war is over.\" In August 2022, Zelenskyy said that since the beginning of the war in Ukraine, Xi Jinping had refused all his requests for direct talks with him.<ref>{{cite news |date=4 August 2022 |title=Zelenskyy urges China's Xi to help end Russia's war in Ukraine |work=[[Al Jazeera]] |url=https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2022/8/4/zelenskyy-urges-chinas-xi-to-help-end-russias-war-in-ukraine |access-date=26 October 2022}}</ref> He additionally said that while he would like China to take a different approach to the war in Ukraine, he also wanted the relationship to improve every year and said that China and Ukraine shared similar values.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Chew |first=Amy |date=2022-08-04 |title=Exclusive: Zelensky seeks talks with China's Xi to help end Russia's invasion of Ukraine |url=https://www.scmp.com/week-asia/politics/article/3187580/volodymyr-zelensky-seeking-direct-talks-chinas-xi-jinping-help |access-date=2022-10-26 |website=[[South China Morning Post]] |language=en}}</ref>\n\n====South Korea====\n{{Main|China\u2013South Korea relations}}\n\nXi has initially improved relationships with South Korea.<ref name=\"chengli2\" /> Starting in 2017, China's relationship with South Korea soured over the [[Terminal High Altitude Area Defense|Terminal High Altitude Area Defence]] (THAAD), a missile defence system, purchase of the latter. which China sees as a threat but which South Korea says is a defence measure against North Korea.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Huang |first=Cary |date=2 April 2017 |title=Why China's economic jabs at South Korea are self-defeating |language=en |newspaper=[[South China Morning Post]] |url=https://www.scmp.com/week-asia/opinion/article/2083166/opinion-why-chinas-shadow-boycott-south-korea-self-defeating |url-status=live |access-date=29 July 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190729174351/https://www.scmp.com/week-asia/opinion/article/2083166/opinion-why-chinas-shadow-boycott-south-korea-self-defeating |archive-date=29 July 2019}}</ref> Ultimately, South Korea halted the purchase of the THAAD after China imposed unofficial sanctions.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Kim |first1=Christine |last2=Blanchard |first2=Ben |date=31 October 2017 |title=China, South Korea agree to mend ties after THAAD standoff |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-northkorea-missiles-idUSKBN1D003G |access-date=29 August 2022}}</ref> China's relations with South Korea improved again under president [[Moon Jae-in]].<ref>{{Cite web |last=Park |first=Chan-kyong |date=26 January 2021 |title=Xi charms Moon as China and US compete for an ally in South Korea |url=https://www.scmp.com/week-asia/politics/article/3119363/xi-charms-moon-china-and-us-compete-ally-south-korea |access-date=14 August 2022 |website=[[South China Morning Post]] |language=en}}</ref>\n\n====Southeast Asia====\nSince Xi came to power, China has been rapidly building and militarizing islands in the [[South China Sea]], a decision ''Study Times'' of the Central Party School said was personally taken by Xi.<ref name=\":24\">{{cite web |date=May 2009 |title=Journal of Current Chinese Affairs |url=http://www.giga-hamburg.de/dl/download.php?d=%2Fcontent%2Fias%2Farchiv%2Fcds%2Fcds_0905.pdf |url-status=live October 2010 |website=giga-hamburg.de}}</ref> In April 2015, new satellite imagery revealed that China was rapidly constructing an airfield on [[Fiery Cross Reef]] in the [[Spratly Islands]] of the South China Sea.<ref>{{cite news |date=17 April 2015 |title=China building runway in disputed South China Sea island |publisher=[[BBC News]] |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-32331964 U.S. Secretary of Defense [[Ash Carter]] warned the government of Xi to halt its rapid [[Great Wall of Sand|island-building]] in disputed territory in the South China Sea.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Whitlock |first=Craig |date=27 May 2015 |title=Defense secretary's warning to China: U.S. military won't change operations |newspaper=[[The Washington Post]] |archive-date=30 October 2018}}</ref> In November 2014, in a major policy address, Xi called for a decrease in the use of force, preferring dialogue and consultation to solve the current issues plaguing the relationship between China and its South East Asian neighbors.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Miller |first1=Matthew |date=7 September 2019 |title=China's Xi tones down foreign policy rhetoric |archive-date=6 December 2014}}</ref>\n\n====United States====\n{{Main|China\u2013United States relations}}\nXi has called China\u2013United States relations in the contemporary world a \"new type of great-power relations\", a phrase the [[Presidency of Barack Obama|Obama administration]] had been reluctant to embrace.<ref name=\"nikkei2\">{{cite news|url=http://asia.nikkei.com/Politics-Economy/International-Relations/A-new-kind-of-great-power-relationship-No-thanks-Obama-subtly-tells-China|title=A new kind of 'great power relationship'? On China\u2013U.S. relations, Xi said, \"If [China and the United States] are in confrontation, it would surely spell disaster for both countries\".<ref name=\"scmp22\">{{cite August 2019|url-status=live}}</ref>  The U.S. has been critical of Chinese actions in the South China Sea.<ref name=\"nikkei2\" /> In 2014, Chinese hackers compromised the computer system of the [[United States Office of Personnel Management|U.S. Office of Personnel Management]],<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.cnn.com/2017/08/24/politics/fbi-arrests-chinese-national-in-opm-data-breach/index.html|last1=Perez|first1=Evan|title=FBI arrests Chinese national connected to malware used in OPM 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> resulting in the [[Office of Personnel Management data breach|theft]] of approximately 22 million personnel records handled by the office.<ref>{{Cite July 2018|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\n[[File:President Trump's Trip to Asia (37575409684).jpg|thumb|U.S. president Donald Trump arrives in China, 8 November 2017]]\n\nXi has also indirectly spoken out soured after [[Donald Trump]] became president in 2017.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Brown |first=Adrian |date=12 May 2019 |title=China-US trade war: Sino-American ties being torn down brick by brick further deteriorated due to the COVID-19 pandemic.<ref>{{Cite news |date=26 March 2020 |title=Relations between China and America are infected with coronavirus |newspaper=[[The Economist]] which China didn't challenge the U.S. in most instances, while Chinese officials said that they now see China as an \"equal\" to the U.S.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Wei |first1=Lingling |last2=Davis Brisbane summit|G20 summit]] in [[Brisbane]], Australia, 15 November 2014]]\n\n====Foreign trips as paramount leader====\n{{Main|List of international trips made by Xi Jinping}}\nXi made his first foreign trip as China's paramount leader to Russia on 22 March 2013, about a week after he assumed the presidency. He met with President Vladimir Putin and the two leaders discussed trade and energy issues. He then went on to Tanzania, South Africa (where he attended the [[BRICS]] summit in [[Durban]]), and the Republic of the Congo.<ref name=\"russiaafrica2\">{{cite news|url=http://en.people.cn/90883/8189481.html|title=Xi's maiden foreign tour historic, fruitful|last=Wu|first=Liming|date=1 April 2013|work=[[People's Daily]]|access-date=7 September 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190617165730/http://en.people.cn/90883/8189481.html|archive-date=17 June 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> Xi visited the United States at [[Sunnylands]] Estate in California in a 'shirtsleeves summit' with U.S. President Barack Obama in June 2013, although this was not considered a formal state visit.<ref name=\"sunnylands2\">{{cite news|url=http://www.brookings.edu/blogs/up-front/posts/2013/06/10-obama-xi-sunnylands-bush|title=Obama and Xi at Sunnylands: A Good Start|last1=Bush|first1=Richard C. October 2013, Xi attended the [[APEC Summit]] in [[Bali]], Indonesia.\n\nIn March 2014, Xi made a trip to Western Europe visiting the Netherlands, where he attended the [[Nuclear Security Summit]] in [[The Hague]],<ref>{{Cite news |date=24 March 2014 |title=China media: Nuclear summit |language=en-GB |work=BBC News |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-china-26711085 |access-date=13 August Geun-hye]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.korea.net/NewsFocus/Society/view?articleId=120421|title=President Xi, 'Korea-China relations better than ever'|date=4 July 2019|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\n[[File:Xi Jinping in British Parliament.jpg|thumb|Xi, who was on a four-day state visit to the U.K., addressed both [[List of people who have addressed both Houses of state visit to the United States]].<ref>{{cite news|url=http://multimedia.scmp.com/xi-jinping-us-visit/|title=Xi Jinping's US visit: itinerary, issues and name=\"ukvisit2\">{{cite web|url=https://www.royal.uk/china-state-visit-programme|title=China State Visit Programme|date=20 October 2015|website=royal.uk|access-date=29 October 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181029191739/https://www.royal.uk/china-state-visit-programme|archive-date=29 October 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> This followed a visit to China in March 2015 by the [[Prince William, Duke of Cambridge|Duke of Cambridge]]. During the state visit, Xi met [[Queen Elizabeth II]], British prime minister [[David Cameron]] and other dignitaries. Increased customs, trade, and research collaborations between China and the U.K. were discussed, but more informal events also took place including a visit to [[Manchester City]]'s [[Association football|football]] academy.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.manchestereveningnews.co.uk/news/greater-manchester-news/chinese-president-xi-jinping-visit-10315388|title=Chinese president Xi Jinping visit: United fan premier to visit Manchester City's stadium|last=Williams|first=Jennifer|date=23 October 2015|newspaper=[[Manchester Evening News]]|access-date=7 September 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190714065912/https://www.manchestereveningnews.co.uk/news/greater-manchester-news/chinese-president-xi-jinping-visit-10315388|archive-date=14 July 2019|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\nIn March 2016, Xi visited the Czech Republic on his way to the United States. In [[Prague]], he met with the Czech president, prime minister and other representatives to promote relations and economic cooperation between the Czech Republic and the PRC.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-czech-china-idUSKCN0WU01J|title=Czech courtship pays off with landmark visit from Chinese leader|last1=Muller|first1=Robert|date=28 March 2016|publisher=[[Reuters]]|access-date=28 March 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161025050433/https://www.reuters.com/article/us-czech-china-idUSKCN0WU01J|archive-date=25 October 2016|last2=Lopatka|first2=Jan}}</ref> His visit was met by a considerable number of protests by Czechs.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.yahoo.com/news/protests-chinas-xi-arrives-prague-173355899.html|title=Protests as China's Xi arrives in Prague|last=Marchal|first=Jan|date=28 March 2016|publisher=[[Agence France-Presse]]|via=Yahoo News |url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160408223306/https://www.yahoo.com/news/protests-chinas-xi-arrives-prague-173355899.html|archive-date=8 April 2016|access-date=28 March 2016}}</ref>\n\n[[File:2017 G20 Hamburg summit leaders group photo.jpg|thumb|World leaders assemble for \u2033family photo\u2033 at [[2017 G20 Hamburg summit|G20 summit]] in Hamburg]]\n\nIn January 2017, Xi became the first Chinese paramount leader to plan to attend the [[World Economic Forum]] in [[Davos]].<ref name=\":1\">{{Cite news |last1=Merced |first1=Michael J. de la |last2=Goldman |first2=Russell |date=14 January 2017 |title=How Davos Brings the Global Elite Together |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/01/14/world/europe/world-economic-forum-davos-explainer-global-elite-parties.html |access-date=17 October 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> On 17 January, Xi addressed the forum in a high-profile keynote, addressing globalization, the global trade agenda, and China's rising place in the world's economy and international governance; he made a series of pledges about China's defense of \"economic globalization\" and climate change accords.<ref name=\":1\" /><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://cn.nytimes.com/china/20170111/davos-china-xi-jinping-trump/|script-title=zh:\u7784\u51c6\u5168\u7403\u4e8b\u52a1\u9886\u5bfc\u6743\uff0c\u4e60\u8fd1\u5e73\u5c06\u9996\u6b21\u51fa\u5e2d\u8fbe\u6c83\u65af|last=Huang|first=Anwei|date=11 January 2017|newspaper=[[The New York Times]]|trans-title=Aimed At Global Affairs, Xi Jinping Will Attend Davos Conference For First Time|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181231034906/https://cn.nytimes.com/china/20170111/davos-china-xi-jinping-trump/|archive-date=31 December 2018|access-date=29 October 2018}}</ref><ref name=\":3\">{{Cite news|url=http://en.people.cn/n3/2017/0111/c90000-9165250.html|title=Xi first top Chinese leader at Davos|last=Kou|first=Jie|date=11 January 2017|newspaper=[[People's Daily]]|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190617132421/http://en.people.cn/n3/2017/0111/c90000-9165250.html|archive-date=17 June 2019|access-date=29 October 2018}}</ref> Premier Li Keqiang attended the forum in 2015 and Vice-president [[Li Yuanchao]] did so in 2016. During the three-day [[state visit]] to the country in 2017 Xi also visited the [[World Health Organization]], the [[United Nations Office at Geneva|United Nations]] and the [[International Olympic Committee]].<ref name=\":3\" />\n\nOn 20 June 2019, Xi visited [[Pyongyang]], becoming the first Chinese leader to visit North Korea since his predecessor Hu Jintao's visit in 2004.<ref name=\":03\">{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/20/world/asia/xi-jinping-china-north-korea.html|title=Xi Jinping Arrives in North Korea, With Many Eyes on Trump|last=Perlez|first=Jane|date=20 June 2019|newspaper=[[The New York Times]]|access-date=7 September 2019|language=en-US|issn=0362-4331|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190905094512/https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/20/world/asia/xi-jinping-china-north-korea.html|archive-date=5 September 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> On 27 June, he attended the [[2019 G20 Osaka summit|G20 summit in Osaka]].<ref>{{Cite web |last=Miller |first=J. Berkshire |date=1 July 2019 |title=China and Japan's Pragmatic Peace |url=https://foreignpolicy.com/2019/07/01/china-and-japans-pragmatic-peace/ |access-date=14 August 2022 |website=Foreign Policy |language=en-US}}</ref> On 17 January 2020, Xi visited [[Myanmar]], meeting president [[Win Myint]], state councillor [[Aung San Suu Kyi]] and military leader [[Min Aung Hlaing]] in [[Naypyidaw]].<ref>{{Cite web |last=Zhou |first=Laura |date=18 January 2020 |title=Xi wraps up Myanmar visit with string of infrastructure deals |url=https://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy/article/3046694/chinese-president-xi-jinping-wraps-myanmar-visit-string |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=[[South China Morning Post]] |language=en}}</ref>\n\n[[File:SCO meeting (2022-09-16).jpg|thumb|Xi in the 2022 SCO summit, during one of his first travel overseas since the beginning of the COVID-19 pandemic]]\n\nBetween 2020 and 2022, Xi paused foreign travel, speculated to be due to the COVID-19 pandemic.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Areddy |first=James T. |date=21 October 2021 |title=Xi Jinping Hasn't Left China in 21 Months, Keeping Diplomacy Virtual |language=en-US |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/xi-jinping-hasnt-left-china-in-21-months-keeping-diplomacy-virtual-11634826813 |access-date=16 September 2022 |issn=0099-9660}}</ref> On 14 February 2022, Xi visited [[Astana]], [[Kazakhstan]], his first trip overseas since the start of the pandemic, meeting president [[Kassym-Jomart Tokayev]].<ref>{{Cite web |date=14 September 2022 |title=Chinese leader Xi Jinping in Kazakhstan before summit with Putin |url=https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2022/9/14/chinese-leader-xi-jinping-in-kazakhstan-before-summit-with-putin |access-date=16 September 2022 |website=[[Al Jazeera]] |language=en}}</ref> A day later, he visited Uzbekistan to attend the [[2022 SCO summit|2022 Shanghai Cooperation Organisation summit]]. There he met with Central Asian leaders as well as Russian president Vladimir Putin, his first since Russia invaded Ukraine on 24 February 2022.<ref>{{Cite web |date=15 September 2022 |title=Putin thanks China's Xi for his 'balanced' stand on Ukraine |url=https://apnews.com/article/russia-ukraine-putin-japan-india-asia-dbe2a0bda954e06bb8fcb7cccbd39b21 |access-date=16 September 2022 |website=[[Associated Press]] |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |last=Mamatkulov |first=Mukhammadsharif |date=16 September 2022 |title=Xi says 'colour revolutions' must be prevented |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/china/putin-xi-speak-summit-uzbekistan-2022-09-16/ |access-date=16 September 2022}}</ref>\n\nBetween 15-16 November 2022, Xi attended the [[2022 G20 Bali summit|G20 Summit in Bali]], meeting numerous world leaders including the US president [[Joe Biden]], Australian prime minister [[Anthony Albanese|Antony Albanese]], French president [[Emmanuel Macron]]<ref>{{Cite news |date=15 November 2022 |title=G20: Macron calls for China and France to unite against Ukraine war |work=[[Euronews]] |url=https://www.euronews.com/2022/11/15/g20-macron-calls-for-china-and-france-to-unite-against-ukraine-war |access-date=5 December 2022}}</ref> and South Korean president [[Yoon Suk-yeol]].<ref>{{Cite news |last=Sim |first=Dawey |date=15 November 2022 |title=G20: Xi Jinping\u2019s meetings with Australia\u2019s Albanese, South Korea\u2019s Yoon show US allies\u2019 hope to Thailand]], meeting leaders including Japanese prime minister [[Fumio Kishida]],<ref>{{Cite news |last=Liao |first=Olivia |date=18 November 2022 |title=Xi-Kishida Meeting Leaves Tough Issues Unresolved |work=[[Voice of America]] |url=https://www.voanews.com/a/xi-kishida-meeting-leaves-tough-issues-unresolved-/6841310.html |access-date=5 December 2022}}</ref> New Zealand prime minister [[Jacinda Ardern]],<ref>{{Cite news |last=McClure |first=Tess |date=19 November 2022 |title=Jacinda Ardern raises Taiwan with Xi Jinping at Apec meeting |work=[[The Guardian]] |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2022/nov/19/jacinda-ardern-raises-taiwan-with-xi-jinping-at-apec-meeting |access-date=5 December 2022}}</ref> Thai prime minister [[Prayut Chan-o-cha]]<ref>{{Cite news |date=19 November 2022 |title=Prayut in full bilateral talks with Xi after Bangkok Apec summit |work=[[The Nation Thailand]] |url=https://www.nationthailand.com/thailand/general/40022245 |access-date=5 December 2022}}</ref> and US vice president [[Kamala Harris]].<ref>{{Cite news |last=Widakuswara |first=Patsy |date=19 Saudi Arabia|Salman]], and crown prince and prime minister [[Mohammed bin Salman]]. He also met with numerous Arab leaders, including members of the [[Gulf Cooperation Council]].<ref>{{Cite news |last=Gambrell |first=John |date=10 December 2022 |title=China\u2019s Xi vows to buy more Mideast oil as US focus wanes |work=[[Associated Press]] |url=https://apnews.com/article/russia-ukraine-saudi-arabia-qatar-tamim-bin-hamad-al-thani-china-government-bcc9cb57ce11712b1fbf0a9ddcfccf04 |access-date=11 December 2022}}</ref> During the meeting, he signed numerous commercial deals with Saudi Arabia and formally elevated the relationship to comprehensive strategic partnership, highest level in China's formal ranking of relations with other countries.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Kalin |first=Stephen |date=8 December 2022 |title=China\u2019s Xi Jinping Deepens Saudi Ties in Pivotal Trip |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/chinas-xi-jinping-to-meet-saudi-crown-prince-in-pivotal-visit-11670480051 |access-date=11 December 2022}}</ref>\n\n====Belt and Road Initiative====\n{{main|Belt and Road Initiative}}\n[[File:Belt and Road Initiative participant map.svg|thumb|300x300px|Countries that signed cooperation documents related to the Belt and Road Initiative]]\n\nThe Belt and Road Initiative (BRI) was unveiled by Xi in September and October 2013 during visits to Kazakhstan and [[Indonesia]],<ref>{{cite web|url=http://english.gov.cn/news/top_news/2015/04/20/content_281475092566326.htm|title=Chronology of China's Belt and Road Initiative|publisher=[[State Council of the People's Republic of China]]|language=en|access-date=23 September 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180923085510/http://english.gov.cn/news/top_news/2015/04/20/content_281475092566326.htm|archive-date=23 September 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> and was thereafter promoted by Premier Li Keqiang during state visits to Asia and Europe. Xi made the announcement for the initiative while in Astana, Kazakhstan, and called it a \"golden opportunity\".<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://usa.chinadaily.com.cn/china/2013-09/08/content_16952304.htm|title=Xi proposes a 'new Silk Road' with Central Asia|last=Jiao|first=Wu|date=8 September 2013|work=[[China Daily]]|access-date=29 October 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181029232425/http://usa.chinadaily.com.cn/china/2013-09/08/content_16952304.htm|archive-date=29 October 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> BRI has been called Xi's \"signature project\", involving numerous infrastructure development and investment projects throughout Asia, Europe, Africa, and the Americas.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://time.com/5578514/china-xi-jinping-belt-road-corruption-debt/|title=Xi Jinping Says China's Belt and Road Initiative Is Not Saddling Poor Countries With Debt|date=26 April 2019|magazine=[[Time (magazine)|Time]]|access-date=10 January 2020}}</ref> BRI was added to the [[Constitution of the Chinese Communist Party|CCP Constitution]] at the closing session of the [[19th National Congress of the Chinese Communist Party|19th Party Congress]] on 24 October 2017,<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.xinhuanet.com/english/2017-10/24/c_136702025.htm|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180127112204/http://www.xinhuanet.com/english/2017-10/24/c_136702025.htm|url-status=dead|archive-date=27 January 2018|title=\"Belt and Road\" incorporated into CPC Constitution|date=24 October 2017|publisher=[[Xinhua News Agency]]|access-date=11 January 2020}}</ref> further elevating its importance.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Tan |first=Huileng |date=31 October 2017 |title=China wrote Belt and Road Initiative into the party constitution. That makes it riskier than ever |work=[[CNBC]] |publisher= |url=https://www.cnbc.com/2017/10/31/china-wrote-belt-and-road-initiative-into-the-party-constitution.html |access-date=11 January 2020}}</ref> Since the BRI was launched, China became the world's largest lender, lending about $1 trillion dollars in a decade to almost 150 countries. However, by 2022, many BRI projects have stalled, and most of China's debt became held by countries in financial distress, leading the Chinese leaders to adopt a more conservative approach to BRI, dubbed as \"Belt and Road Initiative 2.0\".<ref>{{Cite news |last=Wei |first=Lingling |date=26 September 2022 |title=China Reins In Its Belt and Road Program, $1 Trillion Later |language=en-US |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/china-belt-road-debt-11663961638 |access-date=17 October 2022 |issn=0099-9660}}</ref>\n\n===National security===\nXi has devoted a large amount of work towards national security, calling for a \"holistic national security architecture\" that encompasses \"all aspects of the work of the party and the country\".<ref>{{Cite news |date=30 December 2020 |title=Xi Sees Threats to China's Security Everywhere Heading Into 2021 |language=en |work=[[Bloomberg News]] |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-12-30/xi-sees-threats-to-china-s-security-everywhere-heading-into-2021 |access-date=21 August 2022}}</ref> During a private talk with U.S. president Obama and vice president Biden, he said that China had been a target of \"[[colour revolution]]s\", foreshadowing his focus on national security.<ref name=\":27\">{{Cite news |last1=Buckley |first1=Chris |last2=Myers |first2=Steven Lee |date=6 August 2022 |title=In Turbulent Times, Xi Builds a Security Fortress for China, and Himself |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2022/08/06/world/asia/xi-jinping-china-security.html |access-date=21 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> Since its creation by Xi, the National Security Commission has established local security committees, focusing on dissent.<ref name=\":27\" /> In the name of national security, Xi's government has passed numerous laws including a counterespionage law in 2014,<ref>{{Cite news |date=1 November 2014 |title=China passes counter-espionage law |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-lawmaking-spy-idUSKBN0IL2N520141101 |access-date=21 August 2022}}</ref> national security<ref>{{Cite news |last=Wong |first=Chun Han |date=1 July 2015 |title=China Adopts Sweeping National-Security Law |language=en-US |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=http://www.wsj.com/articles/china-adopts-sweeping-national-security-law-1435757589 |access-date=21 August 2022 |issn=0099-9660}}</ref> and a counterterrorism law in 2015,<ref>{{Cite news |last=Blanchard |first=Ben |date=28 December 2015 |title=China passes controversial counter-terrorism law |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-security-idUSKBN0UA07220151228 |access-date=21 August 2022}}</ref> a [[Cybersecurity Law of the People's Republic of China|cybersecurity law]]<ref>{{Cite web |last=Wagner |first=Jack |date=1 June 2017 |title=China's Cybersecurity Law: What You Need to Know |url=https://thediplomat.com/2017/06/chinas-cybersecurity-law-what-you-need-to-know/ |access-date=21 August 2022 |website=[[The Diplomat]] |language=en-US}}</ref> and a law restricting foreign [[Non-governmental organization|NGOs]] in 2016,<ref>{{Cite news |last=Wong |first=Edward |date=28 April 2015 |title=Clampdown in China Restricts 7,000 Foreign Organizations |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/04/29/world/asia/china-foreign-ngo-law.html |access-date=21 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> a [[National Intelligence Law of the People's Republic of China|national intelligence law]] in 2017,<ref>{{Cite news |date=27 June 2017 |title=China passes tough new intelligence law |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-security-lawmaking-idUSKBN19I1FW |access-date=21 August 2022}}</ref> and a [[Data Security Law of the People's Republic of China|data security law]] in 2021.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Haldane |first=Matt |date=1 September 2021 |title=How China's new data laws will make cross-border business much harder |url=https://www.scmp.com/tech/policy/article/3147040/what-chinas-new-data-laws-are-and-their-impact-big-tech |access-date=21 August 2022 |website=[[South China Morning Post]] |language=en}}</ref> Under Xi, [[Mass surveillance in China|China's mass surveillance network]] has dramatically grown, with comprehensive profiles being built for each citizen.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Mozur |first1=Paul |last2=Xiao |first2=Muyi |last3=Liu |first3=John |date=26 June 2022 |title='An Invisible Cage': How China Is Policing the Future |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2022/06/25/technology/china-surveillance-police.html |access-date=21 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> [[Xinjiang papers|Internal Chinese government documents]] leaked to the press in November 2019 showed that Xi repeatedly discussed about [[Islamic extremism]] in his speeches, likening it to a \"virus\" or a \"drug\" that could be only addressed by \"a period of painful, interventionary treatment.\"<ref name=\":11\" /> However, he also warned against the discrimination against Uyghurs and rejected proposals to eradicate [[Islam in China]], calling that kind of viewpoint \"biased, even wrong\".<ref name=\":11\" />\n\n===Hong Kong===\n[[File:2019-10-01 Demonstration Hong Kong 11.jpg|thumb|[[2019\u201320 Hong Kong protests|Hong Kong protesters]] throw eggs at Xi Jinping's portrait on [[National Day of the People's Republic of China|National Day]]]]\n[[File:\u5e86\u795d\u9999\u6e2f\u56de\u5f52\u7956\u56fd25\u5468\u5e74\u5927\u4f1a\u66a8\u9999\u6e2f\u7279\u522b\u884c\u653f\u533a\u7b2c\u516d\u5c4a\u653f\u5e9c\u5c31\u804c\u5178\u793c 20220701-4.png|thumb|Xi swearing in John Lee as chief executive during the 25th anniversary of Hong Kong's return to China]]\n\nXi has supported and pursued a greater economic integration of [[Hong Kong]] to mainland China through projects such as the [[Hong Kong\u2013Zhuhai\u2013Macau Bridge]].<ref name=\":9\">{{Cite news |last=Bland |first=Ben |date=2 September 2018 |title=Greater Bay Area: Xi Jinping's other grand plan |work=[[Financial Times]] |url=https://www.ft.com/content/fe5976d8-ab81-11e8-94bd-cba20d67390c |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/TNDY2 |archive-date=11 December 2022 |url-access=subscription |url-status=live |access-date=11 January 2020}}</ref> He has pushed for the [[Guangdong-Hong Kong-Macau Greater Bay Area|Greater Bay Area]] project, which aims to integrate Hong Kong, Macau, and nine other cities in [[Guangdong]].<ref name=\":9\" /> Xi's push for greater integration has created fears of decreasing freedoms in Hong Kong.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Yu |first=Verna |date=5 November 2019 |title=China signals desire to bring Hong Kong under tighter control |work=[[The Guardian]] |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2019/nov/05/chinas-xi-jinping-expresses-high-degree-of-trust-in-hong-kongs-carrie-lam |access-date=11 January 2020}}</ref> Xi has supported the [[Government of Hong Kong|Hong Kong Government]] and [[Chief Executive of Hong Kong|chief executive]] [[Carrie Lam]] against the protesters in the [[2019\u201320 Hong Kong protests]].<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Sin |first1=Noah |last2=Kwok |first2=Donny |date=16 December 2019 |title=China's Xi vows support for Hong Kong leader during 'most difficult' time |publisher=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-hongkong-protests/chinas-xi-vows-support-for-hong-kong-leader-during-most-difficult-time-idUSKBN1YK025 |access-date=11 January 2020}}</ref> He has defended the [[Hong Kong Police Force|Hong Kong police's]] use of force, saying that \"We sternly support the Hong Kong police to take forceful actions in enforcing the law, and the Hong Kong judiciary to punish in accordance with the law those who have committed violent crimes.\"<ref>{{Cite news |last=Zhou |first=Laura |date=14 November 2019 |title=Xi Jinping again backs Hong Kong police use of force in stopping unrest |work=[[South China Morning Post]] |url=https://www.scmp.com/news/china/politics/article/3037811/xi-jinping-again-backs-hong-kong-police-use-force-stopping |access-date=11 January 2020}}</ref> While visiting [[Macau]] on 20 December 2019 as part of the 20th anniversary of its return to China, Xi warned of foreign forces interfering in Hong Kong and Macau,<ref>{{Cite news |date=20 December 2019 |title=China's Xi warns of 'foreign forces' at Macao anniversary |publisher=[[Deutsche Welle]] |url=https://www.dw.com/en/chinas-xi-warns-of-foreign-forces-at-macao-anniversary/a-51747054 |access-date=11 January 2020}}</ref> while also hinting that Macau could be a model for Hong Kong to follow.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Siu |first1=Phila |last2=Cheung |first2=Gary |date=19 December 2019 |title=Xi Jinping seen as indirectly lecturing Hong Kong as he tells Macau residents to make 'positive voices' heard and resolve problems with rationality |work=[[South China Morning Post]] |url=https://www.scmp.com/news/hong-kong/politics/article/3042846/macau-handover-anniversary-xi-jinping-tells-residents-make |access-date=11 January 2020}}</ref>\n\nIn 2020, the Standing Committee of the National People's Congress (NPCSC) passed a [[Hong Kong national security law|national security law]] in Hong Kong that dramatically expanded government clampdown over the opposition in the city.<ref name=\":20\">{{Cite news |last1=Buckley |first1=Chris |last2=Wang |first2=Vivian |last3=Ramzy |first3=Austin |date=28 June 2021 |title=Crossing the Red Line: Behind China's Takeover of Hong Kong |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2021/06/28/world/asia/china-hong-kong-security-law.html |access-date=13 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> This was seem as the culmination of a long-term project under Xi to further closely integrate Hong Kong with the mainland.<ref name=\":20\" /> Xi visited Hong Kong as president in 2017 and 2022, in the 20th and 25th anniversary of the handover of Hong Kong respectively.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Yip |first1=Martin |last2=Fraser |first2=Simon |date=30 June 2022 |title=China's President Xi arrives in Hong Kong for handover anniversary |language=en-GB |work=[[BBC News]] |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-china-61991980 |access-date=13 August 2022}}</ref> In [[2022 Xi Jinping visit to Hong Kong|his 2022 visit]], he swore in [[John Lee (government official)|John Lee]] as chief executive, a former police officer that was backed by the Chinese government to expand control over the city.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Ioanes |first=Ellen |date=2 July 2022 |title=How Xi Jinping tightened his grip on Hong Kong, 25 years after the handover |url=https://www.vox.com/2022/7/2/23192550/xi-hong-kong-john-lee-china |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=[[Vox (website)|Vox]] |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |last1=Chan |first1=Ho-him |last2=Riordan |first2=Primrose |date=8 May 2022 |title=Beijing-backed hardliner John Lee chosen as Hong Kong's next leader |work=[[Financial Times]] |url=https://www.ft.com/content/a6466afa-0981-4a82-9787-8c630651d44f |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/EEukK |archive-date=11 December 2022 |url-access=subscription |url-status=live |access-date=13 August 2022}}</ref> While in the city, he said Hong Kong had moved from \"chaos\" to \"stability\".<ref>{{Cite web |last1=Chan |first1=Minnie |last2=Zheng |first2=William |date=1 July 2022 |title=Xi praises Hong Kong PLA garrison for city's transition from 'chaos' to 'stability' |url=https://www.scmp.com/news/china/politics/article/3183862/xi-praises-hong-kong-pla-garrison-citys-transition-chaos |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=[[South China Morning Post]] |language=en}}</ref> Since John Lee became chief executive, Hong Kong government officials including Lee himself have shown public displays of loyalty towards Xi, similar to the mainland but previously unheard in the city.<ref name=\":20\" />\n\n===Human rights===\n{{main|Human rights in China|Uyghur genocide|Antireligious campaigns in China}}\n\nAccording to the [[Human Rights Watch]], Xi has \"started a broad and sustained offensive on human rights\" since he became leader in 2012.<ref>{{Cite book|url=https://www.hrw.org/world-report/2018/country-chapters/china-and-tibet|title=World Report 2018: Rights Trends in China|chapter=China: Events of 2017 |date=9 January 2018|publisher=[[Human Rights Watch]]|language=en|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190828203028/https://www.hrw.org/world-report/2018/country-chapters/china-and-tibet|archive-date=28 August 2019|access-date=7 September 2019}}</ref> The HRW also said that repression in China is \"at its worst level since the Tiananmen Square massacre.\"<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/asia/china-repression-freedom-police-censorship-tiananmen-square-human-rights-watch-a8732501.html|title=Repression in China at worst level since Tiananmen Square, HRW warns|last=Withnall|first=Adam|date=17 January 2019|newspaper=[[The Independent]]|language=en|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190524133120/https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/asia/china-repression-freedom-police-censorship-tiananmen-square-human-rights-watch-a8732501.html|archive-date=24 May 2019|access-date=7 September 2019}}</ref> Since taking power, Xi has cracked down on grassroots activism, with hundreds being detained.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.ft.com/content/b4de464a-7242-11e9-bf5c-6eeb837566c5 |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/xmsYf |archive-date=11 December 2022 |url-access=subscription |url-status=live|title=China widens crackdown against grassroot activists|date=9 May 2019|work=[[Financial Times]]|access-date=11 January 2020}}</ref> He presided over the [[709 crackdown]] on 9 July 2015, which saw more than 200 lawyers, legal assistants and human rights activists being detained.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/blogs-china-blog-39974953|title=Wang Quanzhang: The lawyer who simply vanished|last=Sudworth|first=John|date=22 May 2017|publisher=[[BBC News]]|access-date=11 January 2020}}</ref> His term has seen the arrest and imprisonment of activists such as [[Xu Zhiyong]], as well as numerous others who identified with the [[New Citizens' Movement]]. Prominent legal activist [[Pu Zhiqiang]] of the [[Weiquan movement]] was also arrested and detained.<ref name=\"afp2\">{{cite news|url=https://www.bangkokpost.com/world/419842/chinese-dream-turns-sour-for-activists-under-xi-jinping|title=Chinese dream turns sour for activists under Xi Jinping|date=10 July 2014|newspaper=[[Bangkok Post]]|access-date=17 July 2014}}</ref>\n\nIn 2017, the local government of the [[Jiangxi|Jiangxi province]] told [[Christianity in China|Christians]] to replace their pictures of [[Jesus]] with Xi Jinping as part of a general campaign on unofficial churches in the country.<ref name=\"scmpJesus\">{{Cite news|url=https://www.scmp.com/news/china/policies-politics/article/2119699/praise-xi-jinping-not-jesus-escape-poverty-christian|title=Replace pictures of Jesus with Xi to escape poverty, Chinese villagers urged|last=Gan|first=Nectar|date=14 November 2017|newspaper=[[South China Morning Post]]|language=en|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190717174448/https://www.scmp.com/news/china/policies-politics/article/2119699/praise-xi-jinping-not-jesus-escape-poverty-christian|archive-date=17 July 2019|access-date=26 July 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/worldviews/wp/2017/11/14/jesus-wont-save-you-president-xi-jinping-will-chinese-christians-told/|title=Jesus won't save you \u2013 President Xi Jinping will, Chinese Christians told|last=Denyer|first=Simon|date=14 November 2017|newspaper=[[The Washington Post]]|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190531100111/https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/worldviews/wp/2017/11/14/jesus-wont-save-you-president-xi-jinping-will-chinese-christians-told/|archive-date=31 May 2019|access-date=7 September 2019}}</ref><ref name=\"guardianJesus\">{{Cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2018/sep/28/we-are-scared-but-we-have-jesus-china-and-its-war-on-christianity|title='We are scared, but we have Jesus': China and its war on Christianity|last=Haas|first=Benjamin|date=28 September 2018|work=[[The Guardian]]|access-date=7 September
