August 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> According to local social media, officials \"transformed them from believing in religion to believing in the party\".<ref name=\"scmpJesus\" /> According to activists, \"Xi is waging the most severe systematic [[Christianity in China#Restrictions and international interest|suppression of Christianity]] in the country since religious freedom was written into the Chinese constitution in 1982\", and according to pastors and a group that monitors religion in China, has involved \"destroying crosses, burning bibles, shutting churches and ordering followers to sign papers renouncing their faith\".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.apnews.com/c09b2ee4b71540c8a7fd6178820c5970|title=Group: Officials destroying crosses, burning bibles in China|last=Bodeen|first=Christopher|date=10 September 2018|publisher=[[Associated Press]]|access-date=7 September 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191008144601/https://www.apnews.com/c09b2ee4b71540c8a7fd6178820c5970|archive-date=8 October 2019|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\nFollowing several terrorist attacks in [[Xinjiang]] in 2013 and 2014, Xi launched the [[Strike Hard Campaign Against Violent Terrorism]] in 2014, which involved mass detention, and surveillance of ethnic [[Uyghurs]] there.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.ft.com/content/48508182-d426-11e9-8367-807ebd53ab77 |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/dHIC3 |archive-date=11 December 2022 |url-access=subscription |url-status=live|title=Fear and oppression in Xinjiang: China's war on Uighur culture|last=Shepherd|first=Christian|date=12 September 2019|work=[[Financial Times]]|access-date=19 January 2020}}</ref><ref name=\":11\" /> Xi made an inspection tour in Xinjiang between 27 and 30 April in 2014.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://english.agri.gov.cn/news/dqnf/201405/t20140504_21806.htm|title=President Xi Jinping makes inspection tour in Xinjiang|date=4 May 2014|access-date=7 April 2020|publisher=[[Ministry of Agriculture of the People's Republic of China]] (from [[Xinhua News Agency]])|quote=Xi made an inspection tour in Xinjiang from April 27 to 30.}}</ref> The program was massively expanded in 2017.<ref>{{cite news |title=Concentration camps and forced labor: China's repression of the Uighurs, explained |url=https://www.vox.com/2020/7/28/21333345/uighurs-china-internment-camps-forced-labor-xinjiang |work=Vox |date=25 September 2020}}</ref> As of 2020, China is holding 1.8 million people, mostly Uyghurs but also including other ethnic and religious minorities, in [[Xinjiang internment camps|internment camps in Xinjiang]].<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Nebehay |first1=Stephanie |date=14 March 2019 |title=1.5 million Muslims could be detained in China's Xinjiang: academic |newspaper=Reuters |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-xinjiang-rights/15-million-muslims-could-be-detained-in-chinas-xinjiang-academic-idUSKCN1QU2MQ |access-date=11 August 2022}}</ref> Various human rights groups and former inmates have described the camps as \"concentration camps\", where Uyghurs and other minorities have been forcibly assimilated into China's majority [[Han Chinese|ethnic Han]] society.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2019/jul/11/more-than-20-ambassadors-condemn-chinas-treatment-of-uighurs-in-xinjiang|title=More than 20 ambassadors condemn China's treatment of Uighurs in Xinjiang|date=11 July 2019|newspaper=[[The Guardian]]|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190711031342/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2019/jul/11/more-than-20-ambassadors-condemn-chinas-treatment-of-uighurs-in-xinjiang|archive-date=11 July 2019|access-date=11 July 2019}}</ref> This program has been called a [[Uyghur genocide|genocide]] by some observers, while [[UN Human Rights Office report on Xinjiang|a report]] by the [[Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights|UN Human Rights Office]] said they may amount to crimes against humanity.<ref>{{cite news |date=10 December 2021 |title=China's Xi responsible for Uyghur 'genocide', unofficial tribunal says |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/china/chinas-xi-responsible-uyghur-genocide-unofficial-tribunal-says-2021-12-10/ |access-date=24 October 2022}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |date=1 September 2022 |title=U.N. says China may have committed crimes against humanity in Xinjiang |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/china/outgoing-un-human-rights-chief-says-serious-human-rights-violations-committed-2022-08-31/ |access-date=24 October 2022}}</ref> [[Xinjiang papers|Internal Chinese government documents]] leaked to the press in November 2019 showed that Xi personally ordered a security crackdown in Xinjiang, saying that the party must show \"absolutely no mercy\" and that officials use all the \"weapons of the [[people's democratic dictatorship]]\" to suppress those \"infected with the virus of extremism\".<ref name=\":11\">{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2019/11/16/world/asia/china-xinjiang-documents.html|title='Absolutely No Mercy': Leaked Files Expose How China Organized Mass Detentions of Muslims|last1=Ramzy|first1=Austin|last2=Buckley|first2=Chris|date=16 November 2019|newspaper=[[The New York Times]]|access-date=6 December 2019}}</ref><ref name=\"hongkongFPHuawei\">{{cite news|url=https://www.hongkongfp.com/2020/01/19/huaweis-human-rights-record-needs-scrutiny-britain-signs-5g-contracts/|title=Huawei's human rights record needs scrutiny before Britain signs 5G contracts|last=Tugendhat|first=Tom|date=19 January 2020|newspaper=[[Hong Kong Free Press]]|access-date=19 January 2020}}</ref> Xi's exact role in the building of internment camps has not been publicly reported, though he's widely believed to be behind them and his words have been the source for major justifications in the crackdown in Xinjiang.<ref name=\":23\" /><ref>{{Cite news |last=Chin |first=Josh |date=30 November 2021 |title=Leaked Documents Detail Xi Jinping's Extensive Role in Xinjiang Crackdown |language=en-US |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/leaked-documents-detail-xi-jinpings-extensive-role-in-xinjiang-crackdown-11638284709 |access-date=13 August 2022 |issn=0099-9660}}</ref> In the [[Xinjiang Police Files]] leaked in 2022, a document quoting Minister of Public Security [[Zhao Kezhi]] suggested that Xi had been aware of the internment camps.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Zenz |first=Adrian |date=24 May 2022 |title=Public Security Minister's Speech Describes Xi Jinping's Direction of Mass Detentions in Xinjiang |url=https://www.chinafile.com/reporting-opinion/features/public-security-ministers-speech-describes-xi-jinpings-direction-of-mass |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=ChinaFile |language=en}}</ref>\n\n===COVID-19 pandemic===\n{{See also|Chinese government response to COVID-19|COVID-19 pandemic in mainland China}}On 20 January 2020, Xi commented for the first time on the emerging [[COVID-19 pandemic]] in Wuhan, and ordered \"efforts to curb the spread\" of the virus.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Griffiths |first=James |date=17 February 2020 |title=Did Xi Jinping know about the coronavirus outbreak earlier than first suggested? |url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/02/17/asia/china-coronavirus-xi-jinping-intl-hnk/index.html |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=[[CNN]]}}</ref> He gave premier Li Keqiang some responsibility over the COVID-19 response, in what has been suggested by ''The Wall Street Journal'' was an attempt to potentially insulate himself from criticism if the response failed.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Page |first=Jeremy |date=27 January 2020 |title=China's Xi Gives His No. 2 a Rare Chance to Shine in Coronavirus Fight, With Risks for Both |language=en-US |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/chinas-xi-gives-his-no-2-a-rare-chance-to-shine-in-coronavirus-fight-with-risks-for-both-11580138767 |access-date=13 August 2022 |issn=0099-9660}}</ref> The government initially responded to the pandemic with a lockdown and censorship, with the initial response causing widespread backlash within China.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Griffiths |first=James |title=Wuhan is the latest crisis to face China's Xi, and it's exposing major flaws in his model of control |url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/01/23/asia/wuhan-china-coronavirus-sars-response-intl-hnk/index.html |access-date=29 August 2022 |website=[[CNN]]|date=24 January 2020 }}</ref> He met with [[Tedros Adhanom Ghebreyesus]], the director-general of the World Health Organization (WHO), on 28 January.<ref name=\":15\">{{Cite web |last=Steger |first=Isabella |date=10 February 2020 |title=Xi Jinping emerges to meet the people for the first time in China's coronavirus outbreak |url=https://qz.com/1799914/xi-jinping-appears-in-public-after-long-absence-during-coronavirus/ |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=[[Quartz (publication)|Quartz]] |language=en}}</ref> ''[[Der Spiegel]]'' reported that in January 2020 Xi pressured Tedros Adhanom to hold off on issuing a [[Public Health Emergency of International Concern|global warning]] about the outbreak of COVID-19 and hold back information on human-to-human transmission of the virus, allegations denied by the WHO.<ref>{{cite news |date=10 May 2020 |title=WHO dementiert Telefongespr\u00e4ch mit Chinas Pr\u00e4sident |language=de |website=[[Der Spiegel]] |url=https://www.spiegel.de/politik/ausland/corona-ausbruch-who-dementiert-telefongespraech-mit-chinas-praesident-a-37678f1c-6960-453c-a317-8ef9feed8b7c}}</ref> On 5 February, Xi met with Cambodian prime minister [[Hun Sen]] in Beijing, the first foreign leader allowed into China since the outbreak.<ref name=\":15\" /> After the COVID-19 outbreak got under control in Wuhan, Xi visited the city on 10 March.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Yew |first1=Lun Tian |last2=Se |first2=Young Lee |date=10 March 2022 |title=Xi visits Wuhan, signaling tide turning in China's coronavirus battle |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-china-idUSKBN20X01F |access-date=13 August 2022}}</ref> \n\n[[File:Sergio Mattarella and Xi Jinping 2019.jpg|left|thumb|225x225px|Italian president [[Sergio Mattarella]] with Xi in March 2019]]\n\nAfter getting the outbreak in Wuhan under control, Xi has favoured what has officially been termed \"dynamic [[Zero-COVID|zero-COVID policy]]\"<ref>{{Cite web |last=Cao |first=Desheng |title=Xi: Dynamic zero-COVID policy works |url=https://www.chinadaily.com.cn/a/202206/30/WS62bcd80ea310fd2b29e6962b.html |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=[[China Daily]]}}</ref> that aims to control and suppress the virus as much as possible within the country's borders. This has involved local lockdowns and mass-testing.<ref name=\":19\">{{Cite news |last=Wong |first=Chun Han |date=25 July 2022 |title=China's Zero-Covid Policy Drags on Vaccination Drive |language=en-US |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/chinas-zero-covid-policy-drags-on-vaccination-drive-11658745899 |access-date=13 August 2022 |issn=0099-9660}}</ref> While initially credited for China's suppression of the COVID-19 outbreak, the policy was later criticized by foreign and some domestic observers for being out of touch with the rest of the world and taking a heavy toll on the economy.<ref name=\":19\" /> This approach has especially come under criticism during a 2022 lockdown on Shanghai, which forced millions to their homes and damaged the city's economy,<ref>{{Cite web |last=Davidson |first=Helen |date=10 June 2022 |title=Xi Jinping says 'persistence is victory' as Covid restrictions return to Shanghai and Beijing |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2022/jun/10/xi-jinping-says-persistence-is-victory-as-covid-restrictions-return-to-shanghai-and-beijing |access-date=29 August 2022 |website=[[The Guardian]] |language=en}}</ref> denting the image of [[Li Qiang]], close Xi ally and Party secretary of the city.<ref>{{Cite web |last1=Hadano |first1=Tsukasa |last2=Doi |first2=Noriyuki |date=29 June 2022 |title=Xi ally Li Qiang keeps Shanghai party chief job, but star fades |url=https://asia.nikkei.com/Politics/Xi-ally-Li-Qiang-keeps-Shanghai-party-chief-job-but-star-fades |access-date=29 August 2022 |website=[[Nikkei Asia]] |language=en-GB}}</ref> Conversely, Xi has said that the policy was designed to protect people's life safety.<ref>{{Cite web |last1=Cai |first1=Jane |last2=Tang |first2=Frank |date=29 June 2022 |title=China to press on with 'zero Covid', despite economic risks: Xi |url=https://www.scmp.com/news/china/politics/article/3183550/china-press-zero-covid-despite-economic-risks-president-xi |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=[[South China Morning Post]] |language=en}}</ref> On 23 July 2022, the [[National Health Commission]] reported that Xi and other top leaders have taken the local COVID-19 vaccines.<ref>{{Cite news |date=23 July 2022 |title=Covid in China: Xi Jinping and other leaders given domestic vaccine |language=en-GB |work=[[BBC News]] |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-china-62279377 |access-date=13 August 2022}}</ref>\n\nAt the 20th CCP Congress, Xi confirmed the continuation of the zero-COVID policy,<ref>{{cite news |last=McDonell |first=Stephen |date=16 October 2022 |title=Xi Jinping speech: Zero-Covid and zero solutions |work=[[BBC News]] |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-china-63274391 |access-date=11 November 2022}}</ref> though China started a limited easing of the policies in the following weeks.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Ramzy |first=Austin |date=11 November 2022 |title=China Eases Zero-Covid Rules as Economic Toll and Frustrations Mount |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/china-eases-some-covid-19-rules-even-as-cases-pass-10-000-11668150369 |access-date=11 November 2022}}</ref> In November 2022, protests broke out against China's COVID-19 policies, with a [[2022 \u00dcr\u00fcmqi fire|fire in a high rise in \u00dcr\u00fcmqi]] being the trigger.<ref name=\":40\">{{Cite news |last=Che |first=Chang |last2=Buckley |first2=Chris |last3=Chien |first3=Amy Chang |last4=Dong |first4=Joy |date=2022-12-05 |title=China Stems Wave of Protest, but Ripples of Resistance Remain |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2022/12/05/world/asia/china-covid-protests.html |access-date=2022-12-05 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> The protests were held in multiple major cities, with some of the protestors demanding the end of Xi's and CCP's rule.<ref name=\":40\" /> The protests were mostly suppressed by the government by December,<ref name=\":40\" /> while the government started further easing the COVID-19 controls after the protests.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Olcott |first=Eleanor |last2=Mitchell |first2=Tom |date=4 December 2022 |title=Chinese cities ease Covid restrictions following nationwide protests |work=[[Financial Times]] |url=https://www.ft.com/content/bfbc7afb-3994-4e4c-b649-ca791675b296 |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/7FoRR |archive-date=11 December 2022 |url-access=subscription |url-status=live |access-date=5 December 2022}}</ref> On 7 December 2022, China announced large changes to its COVID-19 policy, including allowing quarantine at home for mild infections, reducing of [[Polymerase chain reaction|PCR testing]], and decreasing the power of local officials to implement lockdowns.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Che |first=Chang |last2=Chien |first2=Amy Chang |last3=Stevenson |first3=Alexandra |date=2022-12-07 |title=What Has Changed About China\u2019s \u2018Zero Covid\u2019 Policy |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2022/12/07/world/asia/china-zero-covid-changes.html |access-date=2022-12-08 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref>\n\n===Environmental policy===\n{{Main|Environmental policy in China}}\n[[File:Vladimir Putin met with Xi Jinping in advance of 2022 Beijing Winter Olympics (1).jpg|thumb|Russian president [[Vladimir Putin]] in Beijing with Xi, 2022]]\n\nIn September 2020, Xi announced that China will \"strengthen its 2030 climate target (NDC), peak emissions before 2030 and aim to achieve [[carbon neutrality]] before 2060\".<ref name=\":38\" /> If accomplished, this would lower the expected rise in global temperature by 0.2\u20130.3&nbsp;\u00b0C \u2013 \"the biggest single reduction ever estimated by the Climate Action Tracker\".<ref name=\":38\">{{cite web |date=23 September 2020 |title=China going carbon neutral before 2060 would lower warming projections by around 0.2 to 0.3 degrees C |url=https://climateactiontracker.org/press/china-carbon-neutral-before-2060-would-lower-warming-projections-by-around-2-to-3-tenths-of-a-degree/ |access-date=27 September 2020 |website=[[Climate Action Tracker]]}}</ref> Xi mentioned the link between the COVID-19 pandemic and nature destruction as one of the reasons for the decision, saying that \"Humankind can no longer afford to ignore the repeated warnings of nature.\"<ref>{{cite news |date=23 September 2020 |title=China, the world's top global emitter, aims to go carbon-neutral by 2060 |work=[[ABC News (Australia)|ABC News]] |publisher= |url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-09-23/china-world-top-global-emitter-aims-carbon-neutral-by-2060/12691974 |access-date=29 September 2020}}</ref> On 27 September, Chinese scientists presented a detailed plan how to achieve the target.<ref>{{cite news |date=29 September 2020 |title=China's top climate scientists unveil road map to 2060 goal |newspaper=[[The Japan Times]] |agency=[[Bloomberg News]] |url=https://www.japantimes.co.jp/news/2020/09/29/asia-pacific/science-health-asia-pacific/china-climate-change-road-map-2060/ |access-date=29 September 2020}}</ref> In September 2021, Xi announced that China will not build \"coal-fired power projects abroad, which was said to be potentially \"pivotal\" in reducing emissions. The Belt and Road Initiative did not include financing such projects already in the first half of 2021.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Brant |first1=Robin |date=22 September 2021 |title=China pledges to stop building new coal energy plants abroad |work=[[BBC News]] |publisher= |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-china-58647481 |access-date=29 September 2021}}</ref>\n\nXi Jinping did not attend [[2021 United Nations Climate Change Conference|COP26]] personally. However, a Chinese delegation led by climate change envoy [[Xie Zhenhua (politician)|Xie Zhenhua]] did attend.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Faulconbridge |first=Guy |date=15 October 2021 |title=China's Xi will not attend COP26 in person, UK PM Johnson told |work=[[Reuters]] |publisher= |url=https://www.reuters.com/business/environment/chinas-xi-snub-cop26-uk-pm-johnson-told-times-2021-10-15/ |access-date=20 August 2022}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |last=Harvey |first=Fiona |date=10 November 2021 |title=China's top Cop26 delegate says it is taking 'real action' on climate targets |work=[[The Guardian]] |url=https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2021/nov/10/chinas-top-cop26-delegate-says-it-is-taking-real-action-on-climate-targets |access-date=11 November 2022}}</ref> During the conference, the United States and China agreed on a framework to reduce [[GHG emission]] by co-operating on different measures.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Volcovici |first1=Valeria |last2=James |first2=William |last3=Spring |first3=Jake |date=11 November 2021 |title=U.S. and China unveil deal to ramp up cooperation on climate change |work=[[Reuters]] |publisher= |url=https://www.reuters.com/business/cop/china-us-make-joint-statement-cop26-climate-summit-2021-11-10 |access-date=11 November 2021}}</ref>\n\n===Governance style===\nKnown as a very secretive leader, little is known publicly about how Xi makes political decisions, or how he came to power.<ref name=\":36\">{{Cite news |date=28 September 2022 |title=An investigation into what has shaped Xi Jinping's thinking |newspaper=[[The Economist]] |url=https://www.economist.com/briefing/2022/09/28/an-investigation-into-what-has-shaped-xi-jinpings-thinking |access-date=30 September 2022 |issn=0013-0613}}</ref><ref name=\":28\">{{Cite news |last=Myers |first=Steven Lee |date=5 March 2018 |title=Behind Public Persona, the Real Xi Jinping Is a Guarded Secret |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2018/03/05/world/asia/xi-jinping-china-leader.html |access-date=13 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> Xi's speeches generally get released months or years after they are made.<ref name=\":36\" /> Xi has also never given a press conference since becoming paramount leader, except in rare joint press conferences with foreign leaders.<ref name=\":36\" /><ref>{{Cite web |last=McGregor |first=Richard |date=21 August 2022 |title=Xi Jinping's Radical Secrecy |url=https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2022/08/china-xi-jinping-biography-opacity/671195/ |access-date=21 August 2022 |website=[[The Atlantic]] |language=en}}</ref> ''The Wall Street Journal'' reported that Xi prefers micromanaging in governance, in contrast to previous leaders such as Hu Jintao who left details of major policies to lower-ranking officials.<ref name=\":21\" /> Reportedly, ministerial officials try to get Xi's attention in various ways, with some creating slide shows and audio reports. ''The Wall Street Journal'' also reported that Xi created a performance-review system in 2018 to give evaluations on officials on various measures, including loyalty.<ref name=\":21\" /> According to ''The Economist'', Xi's orders have generally been vague, leaving lower level officials to interpret his words.<ref name=\":23\">{{Cite news |title=Even in secret, China's leaders speak in code |newspaper=[[The Economist]] |url=https://www.economist.com/china/2022/01/01/even-in-secret-chinas-leaders-speak-in-code |access-date=13 August 2022 |issn=0013-0613}}</ref> Chinese state media Xinhua News Agency said that Xi \"personally reviews every draft of major policy documents\" and \"all reports submitted to him, no matter how late in the evening, were returned with instructions the following morning\".<ref name=\":17\">{{Cite news |last=Blachard |first=Ben |date=17 November 2017 |title=Glowing profile cracks door open on private life of China's Xi |language=en |publisher=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-politics-xi-idUSKBN1DH0GA |access-date=9 December 2019}}</ref> Xi called for officials to practice [[Self-criticism (Marxism\u2013Leninism)|self-criticism]] which, according to observers, is in order to appear less corrupt and more popular among the people.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Forde |first1=Brendan |date=9 September 2013 |title=China's 'Mass Line' Campaign |work=[[The Diplomat]] |url=https://thediplomat.com/2013/09/chinas-mass-line-campaign-2/ |url-status=live |access-date=23 June 2018 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180624035650/https://thediplomat.com/2013/09/chinas-mass-line-campaign-2/ |archive-date=24 June 2018}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Levin |first1=Dan |date=20 December 2013 |title=China Revives Mao-Era Self-Criticism, but This Kind Bruises Few Egos |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2013/12/21/world/asia/china-revives-mao-era-self-criticism-but-this-kind-bruises-few-egos.html |url-status=live |access-date=23 June 2018 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180624010400/https://www.nytimes.com/2013/12/21/world/asia/china-revives-mao-era-self-criticism-but-this-kind-bruises-few-egos.html |archive-date=24 June 2018}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Tiezzi |first1=Shannon |date=27 December 2013 |title=The Mass Line Campaign in the 21st Century |work=[[The Diplomat]] |url=https://thediplomat.com/2013/12/the-mass-line-campaign-in-the-21st-century/ |url-status=live |access-date=23 June 2018 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180624010506/https://thediplomat.com/2013/12/the-mass-line-campaign-in-the-21st-century/ |archive-date=24 June 2018}}</ref>\n\n==Political positions==\n{{further|Ideology of the Chinese Communist Party}}\n\n===Chinese Dream===\n{{main|Chinese Dream}}\n[[File:Lujiazui 2016.jpg|thumb|According to the ''[[Qiushi]]'', the Chinese Dream is about Chinese prosperity, collective effort, socialism, and national glory.]]\n\nXi and CCP ideologues coined the phrase \"Chinese Dream\" to describe his overarching plans for China as its leader. Xi first used the phrase during a high-profile visit to the [[National Museum of China]] on 29 November 2012, where he and his Standing Committee colleagues were attending a \"national revival\" exhibition. Since then, the phrase has become the signature political slogan of the Xi era.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.economist.com/leaders/2013/05/04/xi-jinping-and-the-chinese-dream|title=Xi Jinping and the Chinese dream|date=4 May 2013|newspaper=[[The Economist]]|access-date=12 September 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160510092423/http://www.economist.com/news/leaders/21577070-vision-chinas-new-president-should-serve-his-people-not-nationalist-state-xi-jinping|archive-date=10 May 2016|issn=0013-0613}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/asia/china/9935609/Xi-Jinping-calls-for-a-Chinese-Dream.html|title=Xi Jinping calls for a Chinese dream|last1=Moore|first1=Malcolm|date=17 March 2013|work=[[The Daily Telegraph]]|access-date=20 March 2013|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130320072154/http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/asia/china/9935609/Xi-Jinping-calls-for-a-Chinese-Dream.html|archive-date=20 March 2013|url-status=live}}</ref> The origin of the term \"Chinese Dream\" is unclear. While the phrase has been used before by journalists and scholars,<ref name=\"atlantic2\">{{cite news|url=https://www.theatlantic.com/china/archive/2013/05/todays-china-notes-dreams-obstacles/275544/|title=Today's China Notes: Dreams, Obstacles|last=Fallows|first=James|date=3 May 2013|work=[[The Atlantic]]|access-date=7 September 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180712023142/https://www.theatlantic.com/china/archive/2013/05/todays-china-notes-dreams-obstacles/275544/|archive-date=12 July 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> some publications have posited the term likely drew its inspiration from the concept of the [[American Dream]].<ref name=\"economist22\">{{cite news|url=https://www.economist.com/blogs/analects/2013/05/chinese-dream-0|title=The role of Thomas Friedman|last=M.|first=J.|date=6 May 2013|newspaper=[[The Economist]]|access-date=12 September 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171028145059/https://www.economist.com/blogs/analects/2013/05/chinese-dream-0|archive-date=28 October 2017|url-status=live}}</ref> ''[[The Economist]]'' noted the abstract and seemingly accessible nature of the concept with no specific overarching policy stipulations may be a deliberate departure from the jargon-heavy ideologies of his predecessors.<ref name=\":4\">{{Cite news|url=https://www.economist.com/news/briefing/21577063-chinas-new-leader-has-been-quick-consolidate-his-power-what-does-he-now-want-his|title=Chasing the Chinese dream |date=4 May 2013|newspaper=[[The Economist]]|access-date=12 September 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161028080732/http://www.economist.com/news/briefing/21577063-chinas-new-leader-has-been-quick-consolidate-his-power-what-does-he-now-want-his|archive-date=28 October 2016|issn=0013-0613}}</ref> Xi has linked the \"Chinese Dream\" with the phrase \"great rejuvenation of the Chinese nation\".<ref>{{Cite web |last=Tao |first=Xie |date=14 March 2014 |title=Opinion: Is the Chinese dream fantasy or reality? |url=https://www.cnn.com/2014/03/14/world/asia/chinese-dream-anniversary-xi-jinping-president/index.html |access-date=14 August 2022 |website=[[CNN]]}}</ref>{{NoteTag|{{zh|links=no|s=\u4e2d\u534e\u6c11\u65cf\u4f1f\u5927\u590d\u5174}}, which can also be translated as the \"Great Renaissance of the Chinese nation\" or the \"Great revival of the Chinese people\".}}\n\n===Cultural revival===\nIn recent years, top political leaders of the CCP such as Xi have overseen the rehabilitation of ancient Chinese philosophical figures like [[Han Fei]] into the mainstream of Chinese thought alongside [[Confucianism]]. At a meeting with other officials in 2013, he quoted [[Confucius]], saying \"he who rules by virtue is like the Pole Star, it maintains its place, and the multitude of stars pay homage.\" While visiting [[Shandong]], the birthplace of Confucius, in November, he told scholars that the [[Western world]] was \"suffering a crisis of confidence\" and that the CCP has been \"the loyal inheritor and promoter of China's outstanding [[Traditional Chinese culture|traditional culture]].\"<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2014/10/12/world/leader-taps-into-chinese-classics-in-seeking-to-cement-power.html|title=Leader Taps into Chinese Classics in Seeking to Cement Power|last=Buckley|first=Chris|date=12 October 2014|newspaper=[[The New York Times]]|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190912091736/https://www.nytimes.com/2014/10/12/world/leader-taps-into-chinese-classics-in-seeking-to-cement-power.html|archive-date=12 September 2019|access-date=7 September 2019}}</ref>\n\nAccording to several analysts, Xi's leadership has been characterised by a resurgence of the ancient political philosophy [[Legalism (Chinese philosophy)|Legalism]].<ref name=tni-cnl>{{cite journal |last1=Schneider |first1=David K. |title=China's New Legalism |journal=The National Interest |date=2016 |issue=143 |pages=19\u201325 |doi= |jstor=26557304 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |last1=Crane |first1=Sam |title=Why Xi Jinping's China is Legalist, Not Confucian |url=https://chinachannel.org/2018/06/29/legalism/ |website=China Channel |date=29 June 2018 |access-date=24 November 2020 |archive-date=7 November 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201107225951/https://chinachannel.org/2018/06/29/legalism/ |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref name=tdma/> Han Fei gained new prominence with favourable citations; one sentence of Han Fei's that Xi quoted appeared thousands of times in official Chinese media at the local, provincial, and national levels.<ref name=tdma>{{cite news|url=https://thediplomat.com/2015/01/is-chinas-machiavelli-now-its-most-important-political-philosopher/|title=Is 'China's Machiavelli' Now Its Most Important Political Philosopher?|last=Mitchell|first=Ryan Mi|date=16 January 2015|newspaper=[[The Diplomat]]|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190912091739/https://thediplomat.com/2015/01/is-chinas-machiavelli-now-its-most-important-political-philosopher/|archive-date=12 September 2019|access-date=7 September 2019}}</ref> Xi has additionally supported the [[Neo-Confucianism|Neo-Confucian]] philosopher [[Wang Yangming]], telling local leaders to promote him.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Johnson |first=Ian |date=18 October 2017 |title=Forget Marx and Mao. Chinese City Honors Once-Banned Confucian. |language=en-US |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/10/18/world/asia/china-guiyang-wang-yangming-confucian.html |access-date=13 August 2022 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref>\n\nXi has also overseen a revival of traditional Chinese culture, breaking apart from CCP's path, which had often attacked it.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.economist.com/china/2017/08/17/the-communist-party-is-redefining-what-it-means-to-be-chinese|title=The Communist Party is redefining what it means to be Chinese|date=17 August 2017|newspaper=[[The Economist]]|access-date=23 January 2020}}</ref> He has called traditional culture the \"soul\" of the nation and the \"foundation\" of the CCP's culture.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Zi |first=Yang |date=6 July 2016 |title=Xi Jinping and China's Traditionalist Restoration |work=[[The Jamestown Foundation]] |publisher= |url=https://jamestown.org/program/xi-jinping-chinas-traditionalist-restoration/ |access-date=23 January 2020}}</ref> [[Hanfu]], the traditional dress of Han Chinese, has seen a revival under him, associated with the revival of traditional culture.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.afr.com/life-and-luxury/fashion-and-style/why-its-hip-to-be-oldfashioned-in-china-20181129-h18hql|title=China's 'Hanfu' movement is making it hip to be old-fashioned. Here's why.|last=Buckley|first=Chris|date=30 November 2018|work=[[The Australian Financial Review]]|access-date=23 January 2020}}</ref>\n\n===Ideology===\n{{See also|Eight-point Regulation}}\n\nXi has said that \"only socialism can save China\".<ref>{{Cite news |last=Tian |first=Yew Lun |date=9 September 2021 |title=Analysis: Unleashing reforms, Xi returns to China's socialist roots |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/china/unleashing-reforms-xi-returns-chinas-socialist-roots-2021-09-09/ |access-date=17 September 2022}}</ref> Xi has also declared [[Deng Xiaoping]]'s [[socialism with Chinese characteristics]] to be the \"only correct path to realize national rejuvenation\".<ref>{{Cite web |date=9 October 2021 |title=Socialism with Chinese characteristics only correct path toward national rejuvenation: Xi |url=http://ex.chinadaily.com.cn/exchange/partners/82/rss/channel/www/columns/np4922/stories/WS61610570a310cdd39bc6dcc1.html |access-date=17 September 2022 |website=[[China Daily]]}}</ref> According to [[BBC News]], while the CCP was perceived to have abandoned its communist ideology since it initiated [[Chinese economic reform|economic reforms]] in the 1970s, Xi is believed by some observers to be more believing in the \"idea of a communist project\",<ref>{{Cite news |last=McDonell |first=Stephen |date=22 September 2021 |title=Changing China: Xi Jinping's effort to return to socialism |language=en-GB |work=[[BBC News]] |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/business-58579831 |access-date=17 September 2022}}</ref> being described as a [[Marxist\u2013Leninist]] by former Australian prime minister [[Kevin Rudd]].<ref>{{Cite news |last=Rudd |first=Kevin |author-link=Kevin Rudd |date=10 October 2022 |title=The World According to Xi Jinping |language=en-US |work=[[Foreign Affairs]] |url=https://www.foreignaffairs.com/china/world-according-xi-jinping-china-ideologue-kevin-rudd |access-date=12 October 2022}}</ref> Subscribing to the view that socialism will eventually triumph over capitalism, he has said \"Marx and Engels's analysis of the basic contradictions of capitalist society is not outdated, nor is the historical materialist view that capitalism is bound to die out and socialism bound to win\".<ref name=\":33\">{{Cite web |last=Hancock |first=Tom |date=6 June 2022 |title=Marxism Makes a Comeback in China's Crackdown on 'Disorderly Capital' |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/features/2022-06-06/marxism-makes-a-comeback-in-china-s-crackdown-on-disorderly-capital |access-date=17 September 2022 |website=[[Bloomberg News]]}}</ref> Xi has overseen the increase of \"Socialist Political Economy With Chinese Characteristics\" as a major study topic for academics in China, aiming to decrease the influence of Western-influenced economics.<ref name=\":33\" /> Though he has called a stop to what he considers to be \"disorderly expansion of capital\", he has also said that \"it is necessary to stimulate the vitality of capital of all types, including nonpublic capital, and give full play to its positive role\".<ref name=\":33\" />\n\n{{Quote box\n| quote = China's success proves that socialism is not dead. It is thriving. Just imagine this: had socialism failed in China, had our communist party collapsed like the party in the Soviet Union, then global socialism would lapse into a long dark age. And communism, like Karl Marx once said, would be a haunting spectre lingering in limbo.\n| source = \u2014 Xi Jinping during a speech in 2018<ref name=\":34\" />\n| align = right\n| width = 25em\n}}\n\nXi has supported greater CCP control over the PRC, saying \"government, the military, society and schools, north, south, east and west \u2013 the party leads them all\".<ref>{{Cite web |last=Gan |first=Nectar |date=25 October 2017 |title=The Communist Party's tighter grip on China in 16 characters |url=https://www.scmp.com/news/china/policies-politics/article/2116836/xi-jinping-thought-communist-partys-tighter-grip-china |access-date=14 August 2022 |website=[[South China Morning Post]] |language=en}}</ref> During the [[100th Anniversary of the Chinese Communist Party|100th anniversary of the CCP]] in 2021, he said that \"without the Communist Party of China, there would be no new China and no national rejuvenation\", and that \"the leadership of the Party is the defining feature of socialism with Chinese characteristics and constitutes the greatest strength of this system\".<ref name=\":34\">{{Cite web |date=1 July 2021 |title=Full text of Xi Jinping's speech on the CCP's 100th anniversary |url=https://asia.nikkei.com/Politics/Full-text-of-Xi-Jinping-s-speech-on-the-CCP-s-100th-anniversary |access-date=14 August 2022 |website=[[Nikkei Asia]] |language=en-GB}}</ref> He has said that China, despite many setbacks, has achieved great progress under the CCP, saying that \"socialism with Chinese characteristics has become the standard-bearer of 21st-century socialist development\".<ref name=\":12bb\">{{Cite web |last=Zheng |first=William |date=16 September 2022 |title=Xi article gives insight into China's direction ahead of party congress |url=https://www.scmp.com/news/china/politics/article/3192677/xi-article-gives-insight-chinas-direction-ahead-party-congress |access-date=17 September 2022 |website=[[South China Morning Post]] |language=en}}</ref> However, he has also warned that it will take a long time for China under the CCP to complete its rejuvenation, and during this timeframe, party members must be vigilant to not let CCP rule collapse.<ref name=\":12bb\" />\n\nXi has ruled out a [[multi-party system]] for China, saying that \"constitutional monarchy, imperial restoration, parliamentarism, a multi-party system and a presidential system, we considered them, tried them, but none worked\".<ref>{{Cite news |date=2 April 2014 |title=Xi says multi-party system didn't work for China |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-politics-xi-idUSBREA3107S20140402 |access-date=13 August 2022}}</ref> However, Xi considers China to be a [[Democracy in China|democracy]], saying that \"China\u2019s [[socialist democracy]] is the most comprehensive, genuine and effective democracy\".<ref name=\":18\">{{Cite web |title=Democracy |url=https://decodingchina.eu/democracy/ |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=Decoding China |language=en-US}}</ref> China's definition of democracy is different from [[liberal democracies]] and is rooted in [[Marxism\u2013Leninism]], and is based on the phrases \"[[people's democratic dictatorship]]\" and \"[[democratic centralism]]\".<ref name=\":18\" /> Xi has additionally coined the term \"whole-process people's democracy\" ({{zh|s=\u5168\u8fc7\u7a0b\u4eba\u6c11\u6c11\u4e3b|labels=no}}), which he said was about having \"the people as masters\".<ref>{{Cite web |last=Chen |first=Stella |date=23 November 2021 |title=Whole-Process Democracy |url=https://chinamediaproject.org/the_ccp_dictionary/whole-process-democracy/ |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=China Media Project |language=en-US}}</ref> Foreign analysts and observers have widely disputed that China is a democracy, saying that it is a one-party authoritarian state and Xi an authoritarian leader.{{refn|name=dictatorandauthoritarian|<ref>{{Cite journal|last=Brady|first=Anne-Marie|date=2015|title=China's Foreign Propaganda Machine|url=https://muse.jhu.edu/content/crossref/journals/journal_of_democracy/v026/26.4.brady.html|journal=Journal of Democracy|language=en|volume=26|issue=4|pages=51\u201359|doi=10.1353/jod.2015.0056|s2cid=146531927|issn=1086-3214}}</ref><ref>{{Cite journal|last=Amako|first=Satoshi|date=2 January 2018|title=China's authoritarian path to development: is democratization possible?, by Liang Tang, Abingdon, Routledge, 2017, 263pp., {{text|ISBN}}: 978-1-138-01647-7|journal=Journal of Contemporary East Asia Studies|volume=7|issue=1|pages=81\u201383|doi=10.1080/24761028.2018.1483700|issn=2476-1028|doi-access=free}}</ref><ref>{{Cite book|last=Tung|first=Hans H.|title=Economic Growth and Endogenous Authoritarian Institutions in Post-Reform China|publisher=Palgrave Macmillan|year=2019|isbn=978-3-030-04828-0|location=|pages=}}</ref><ref>{{Cite journal|last1=Howell|first1=Jude|last2=Pringle|first2=Tim|date=2019|title=Shades of Authoritarianism and State\u2013Labour Relations in China|journal=British Journal of Industrial Relations|language=en|volume=57|issue=2|pages=223\u2013246|doi=10.1111/bjir.12436|s2cid=158485609|issn=1467-8543|url=https://eprints.soas.ac.uk/29847/1/Howell%20and%20Pringle_Shades%20of%20Authoritarianism_British_Journal_of_Industrial_Relations.pdf}}</ref><ref>{{Cite journal|last=D\u00fcben|first=Bj\u00f6rn Alexander|date=3 March 2020|title=Xi Jinping and the End of Chinese Exceptionalism|journal=Problems of Post-Communism|volume=67|issue=2|pages=111\u2013128|doi=10.1080/10758216.2018.1535274|s2cid=158657283|issn=1075-8216}}</ref><ref>{{Cite book|last=Tung|first=Hans H.|title=Economic Growth and Endogenous Authoritarian Institutions in Post-Reform China|publisher=Palgrave Macmillan|year=2019|isbn=978-3-030-04828-0}}</ref>}} Some observers have called Xi a dictator, citing the large centralisation of power around him unseen compared to his predecessors.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Phillips |first=Tom |date=26 February 2018 |title='Dictator for life': Xi Jinping's power grab condemned as step towards tyranny |language=en-US |work=[[The Guardian]] |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2018/feb/26/xi-jinping-china-presidential-limit-scrap-dictator-for-life |access-date=12 August 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |last=Gueorguiev |first=Dimitar |date=4 December 2019 |title=Is China a dictatorship? |language=en-US |newspaper=[[The Washington Post]] |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/12/04/michael-bloomberg-said-china-isnt-dictatorship-is-he-right/ |access-date=14 July 2021 |quote=Yes, Xi Jinping is a dictator.}}</ref>\n\n====Document Number Nine====\n[[Document Number Nine|Document No. 9]], officially the \u2033Communiqu\u00e9 on the Current State of the Ideological Sphere\u2033, is a [[Internal media of the Chinese Communist Party|confidential internal document]] widely circulated within the CCP in 2013 by the [[General Office of the Chinese Communist Party|party's General Office]].<ref>{{cite web |last=Li |first=Bing |date=16 May 2013 |script-title=zh:\u7701\u50a8\u5907\u5c40\u8ba4\u771f\u5b66\u4e60\u8d2f\u5f7b\u843d\u5b9e\u300a\u5173\u4e8e\u5f53\u524d\u610f\u8bc6\u5f62\u6001\u9886\u57df\u60c5\u51b5\u7684\u901a\u62a5\u300b\uff0c\u6e56\u5357\u673a\u5173\u515a\u5efa |trans-title=The Provincial Reserve Bureau Has Carefully Studied and Implemented the \"Notice on the Current Situation of Ideology\" |url=http://www.hndj.gov.cn/html/jgdj/gzkx/2013/5168269.html |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130615122048/http://www.hndj.gov.cn/html/jgdj/gzkx/2013/5168269.html |archive-date=15 June 2013 |access-date=16 October 2013 |website=hndj.gov.cn}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |last=Liang |first=Liming |date=9 May 2013 |script-title=zh:\u897f\u85cf\u5e7f\u7535\u5c40\u53ec\u5f00\u4f20\u8fbe\u5b66\u4e60\u6709\u5173\u6587\u4ef6\u7cbe\u795e\u4f1a\u8bae\uff0c\u4e2d\u56fd\u897f\u85cf\u4e4b\u58f0\u7f51 |trans-title=Tibet Radio and Television Bureau Holds Vigorous Discussion To Study Documents in Concern |url=http://www.vtibet.cn/zhuanti/2013-05/09/cms340592article.shtml |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130615105337/http://www.vtibet.cn/zhuanti/2013-05/09/cms340592article.shtml |archive-date=15 June 2013 |access-date=16 October 2013 |website=vtibet.cn}}</ref> It was published in July 2012.<ref>{{cite web |last=Ren |first=Jie |date=3 July 2012 |script-title=zh:\u5f53\u524d\u6211\u56fd\u610f\u8bc6\u5f62\u6001\u5efa\u8bbe\u9762\u4e34\u7684\u516d\u5927\u6311\u6218--\u7406\u8bba--\u4eba\u6c11\u7f51 |trans-title=Six Major Challenges Facing China's Ideological Construction |url=http://theory.people.com.cn/n/2012/0703/c83855-18430666.html |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121031235702/http://theory.people.com.cn/n/2012/0703/c83855-18430666.html |archive-date=31 October 2012 |access-date=8 September 2019 |work=[[People's Daily]] |language=zh-hans}}</ref> The document officially warns of promoting seven dangerous Western values:<ref>{{Cite web |date=8 November 2013 |title=Document 9: A ChinaFile Translation |url=https://www.chinafile.com/document-9-chinafile-translation |access-date=13 August 2022 |website=ChinaFile |language=en}}</ref>\n\n* Western Constitutional Democracy: an attempt to undermine the current leadership and the socialism with Chinese characteristics system of governance;\n* \"Universal values\" in an attempt to weaken the theoretical foundations of the Party's leadership;\n* Civil society in an attempt to dismantle the ruling party's social foundation;\n* Neoliberalism, attempting to change China's Basic Economic System;\n* West's idea of journalism, challenging China's principle that the media and publishing system should be subject to Party discipline;\n* Historical nihilism, trying to undermine the history of the CCP and of New China; and\n* Questioning Reform and Opening and the socialist nature of socialism with Chinese characteristics.\n\nAlthough it predates Xi Jinping's formal rise to the top party and state posts, the release of this internal document, which has introduced new topics that were previously not \"off-limits\", was being closely associated with Xi Jinping by ''[[The New York Times]]''.<ref name=\"NYT819132\">{{cite news |last=Buckley |first=Christopher |date=19 August 2013 |title=China's New Leadership Takes Hard Line in Secret Memo |work=[[The New York Times]] |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2013/08/20/world/asia/chinas-new-leadership-takes-hard-line-in-secret-memo.html?ref=global-home |url-access=limited |access-date=8 September 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160721050121/http://www.nytimes.com/2013/08/20/world/asia/chinas-new-leadership-takes-hard-line-in-secret-memo.html?ref=global-home |archive-date=21 July 2016}}</ref>\n\n====Xi Jinping Thought====\n{{main|Xi Jinping Thought}}\n[[File:A political slogan on the wall in Longhua District, Shenzhen, Guangdong, China, picture1.jpg|thumb|A billboard promoting [[Xi Jinping Thought]] in [[Shenzhen]]]]\n\nIn September 2017, the CCP Central Committee decided that Xi's political philosophies, generally referred to as \"Xi Jinping Thought on Socialism with Chinese Characteristics for a New Era\", would become part of the Party Constitution.<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://news.xinhuanet.com/politics/2017-09/18/c_1121683516.htm|script-title=zh:\u4e2d\u5171\u4e2d\u592e\u653f\u6cbb\u5c40\u53ec\u5f00\u4f1a\u8bae \u7814\u7a76\u62df\u63d0\u8bf7\u515a\u7684\u5341\u516b\u5c4a\u4e03\u4e2d\u5168\u4f1a\u8ba8\u8bba\u7684\u6587\u4ef6-\u65b0\u534e\u7f51|last1=Liu|first1=Xiaodong|last2=Chen|first2=Yu|date=18 September 2017|publisher=[[Xinhua News Agency]]|language=zh-hans|trans-title=The Political Bureau of the CPC Central Committee Convened to Study the Documents to be Submitted to the Seventh Plenary Session of the 18th CPC Central Committee|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171011094706/http://news.xinhuanet.com/politics/2017-09/18/c_1121683516.htm|archive-date=11 October 2017|access-date=4 October 2017}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=http://chinadigitaltimes.net/2017/09/party-constitution-amendment-signal-xis-power/|title=CCP Constitution Amendment May Signal Xi's Power \u2013 China Digital Times (CDT)|last=Rudolph|first=Josh|date=19 September 2017|work=[[China Digital Times]] (CDT)|access-date=4 October 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171003234252/http://chinadigitaltimes.net/2017/09/party-constitution-amendment-signal-xis-power/|archive-date=3 October 2017|url-status=live}}</ref> Xi first made mention of the \"Thought on Socialism with Chinese Characteristics for a New Era\" in his opening day speech delivered to the [[19th National Congress of the Chinese Communist Party|19th Party Congress]] in October 2017. His Politburo Standing Committee colleagues, in their own reviews of Xi's keynote address at the Congress, prepended the name \"Xi Jinping\" in front of \"Thought\".<ref name=\"xithought2\">{{cite news|url=http://news.xinhuanet.com/english/2017-10/19/c_136689808.htm|title=CPC creates Xi Jinping Thought on Socialism with Chinese Characteristics for a New Era|last1=Zhang|first1=Ling|date=18 October 2017|work=[[Xinhua News Agency]]|access-date=19 October 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171018195301/http://news.xinhuanet.com/english/2017-10/19/c_136689808.htm|archive-date=18 October 2017|url-status=dead}}</ref> On 24 October 2017, at its closing session, the 19th Party Congress approved the incorporation of Xi Jinping Thought into the Constitution of the CCP,<ref name=\"PhillipsGuardian2\" /> while in March 2018, the [[National People's Congress]] changed the state constitution to include Xi Jinping Thought.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Ken |first=Suzuki |date=27 November 2018 |title=China's New \"Xi Jinping Constitution\": The Road to Totalitarianism |url=https://www.nippon.com/en/in-depth/a05803/ |access-date=11 August 2022 |website=nippon.com |language=en}}</ref>\n\n[[File:201901 Xi Jinping's books at Shanghai Library.jpg|left|thumb|''[[The Governance of China]]'' in different languages presented at [[Shanghai Library]]]]\n\nXi himself has described the Thought as part of the broad framework created around [[Socialism with Chinese characteristics]], a term coined by Deng Xiaoping that places China in the [[primary stage of socialism]]. In official party documentation and pronouncements by Xi's colleagues, the Thought is said to be a continuation of [[Marxism\u2013Leninism]], [[Mao Zedong Thought]], Deng Xiaoping Theory, the Three Represents, and the [[Scientific Outlook on Development]], as part of a series of guiding ideologies that embody \"Marxism adopted to Chinese conditions\" and contemporary considerations.<ref name=\"xithought2\" /> It has additionally been described as the \"21st century Marxism\" by two professors in the [[Central Party School of the Chinese Communist Party|Central Party School]] of the CCP.<ref name=\":29\" /> [[Wang Huning]], a top political adviser and a close ally of Xi, has been described as pivotal to developing Xi Jinping Thought.<ref name=\":29\" /> The concepts and context behind Xi Jinping Thought are elaborated in Xi's ''[[The Governance of China]]'' book series, published by the [[Foreign Languages Press]] for an international audience. Volume one was published in September 2014, followed by volume two in November 2017.<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://news.xinhuanet.com/english/2017-11/07/c_136733705.htm|title=Second volume of Xi's book on governance published|last=Yang|first=Yi|date=7 November 2017|publisher=[[Xinhua News Agency]]|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171206143920/http://news.xinhuanet.com/english/2017-11/07/c_136733705.htm|archive-date=6 December 2017|access-date=6 December 2017}}</ref>\n\nAn app for teaching Xi Jinping Thought had become the most popular smartphone app in China in 2019, as the country's ruling CCP launched a new campaign that calls on its cadres to immerse themselves in the political doctrine every day. ''[[Xuexi Qiangguo]]'' is now the most downloaded item on Apple's domestic App Store, surpassing in demand social media apps such as [[WeChat]] and [[TikTok]].<ref name=scmp20100214>{{Cite news|url=https://www.scmp.com/tech/apps-social/article/2186037/chinas-most-popular-app-propaganda-tool-teaching-xi-jinping-thought|title=China's most popular app is a propaganda tool teaching Xi Jinping Thought|last=Huang|first=Zheping|date=14 February 2019|work=[[South China Morning Post]]|access-date=7 September 2019|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190920105809/https://www.scmp.com/tech/apps-social/article/2186037/chinas-most-popular-app-propaganda-tool-teaching-xi-jinping-thought|archive-date=20 September 2019}}</ref> In 2021, the government included Xi Jinping Thought in the curriculum including to students from primary schools to university, which created pushback from parents. For much of the preceding 30 years, political ideology and communist doctrine were not a standard taught in Chinese schools until middle school, and textbooks featured a wider set of Chinese leaders with less emphasis on a single leader like Xi.<ref name=\"irishtimes202108292\">{{cite news |date=29 August 2021 |title=Lessons on Xi Jinping's political philosophy alarm Chinese parents |work=[[Irish Times]] |url=https://www.irishtimes.com/news/world/asia-pacific/lessons-on-xi-jinping-s-political-philosophy-alarm-chinese-parents-1.4659194 |access-date=7 September 2021 |quote=''A campaign to make Chinese children as young as 10 study President Xi Jinping's political philosophy has been labelled by some parents as 'disgusting', and evoked memories of Mao Zedong's personality cult.''}}</ref>\n\n==Personal life==\n===Family===\n[[File:Peng Liyuan, Xi Jinping and Barack Obama in the Lincoln Bedroom.jpg|thumb|Xi Jinping, [[Peng Liyuan]] and U.S. president [[Barack Obama]] in the Lincoln Bedroom]]\n\nXi's first marriage was to [[Ke Lingling]], the daughter of [[Ke Hua]], China's ambassador to the United Kingdom in the early 1980s. They divorced within a few years.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://edition.cnn.com/2012/11/07/world/asia/china-xi-jinping-profile/index.html|title=Xi Jinping: From 'sent-down youth' to China's top|last=Yuan|first=Elizabeth|date=8 November 2012|publisher=[[CNN]]|access-date=8 November 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121108195546/http://edition.cnn.com/2012/11/07/world/asia/china-xi-jinping-profile/index.html|archive-date=8 November 2012}}</ref> The two were said to fight \"almost every day\", and after the divorce Ke moved to England.<ref name=\"newyorker2\" /> In 1987, Xi married the prominent Chinese folk singer [[Peng Liyuan]].<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://articles.latimes.com/2007/oct/23/world/fg-chileaders23|title=China's 'fifth generation' of leaders reflects nation's shifts|last=Magnier|first=Mark|date=23 October 2007|work=[[Los Angeles Times]]|access-date=21 December 2009|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110823133224/http://articles.latimes.com/2007/oct/23/world/fg-chileaders23|archive-date=23 August 2011}}</ref> Xi and Peng were introduced by friends as many Chinese couples were in the 1980s. Xi was reputedly academic during their courtship, inquiring about singing techniques.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://blogs.wsj.com/chinarealtime/2012/02/13/peng-liyuan-meet-chinas-folk-song-singing-first-lady-in-waiting/|title=Meet China's Folk Star First Lady-in-Waiting|last=Page|first=Jeremy|date=12 February 2012|work=[[The Wall Street Journal]]|access-date=7 November 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120511045002/http://blogs.wsj.com/chinarealtime/2012/02/13/peng-liyuan-meet-chinas-folk-song-singing-first-lady-in-waiting/|archive-date=11 May 2012}}</ref> Peng Liyuan, a [[Celebrity|household name]] in China, was better known to the public than Xi until his political elevation. The couple frequently lived apart due largely to their separate professional lives. Peng has played a much more visible role as China's \"first lady\" compared to her predecessors; for example, Peng hosted U.S. First Lady [[Michelle Obama]] on her high-profile visit to China in March 2014.<ref name=\"beech2\">{{cite news|url=http://time.com/33164/michelle-obama-china-beijing-peng-liyuan/|title=Michelle Obama Tours Beijing With China's First Lady|last1=Beech|first1=Hannah|date=21 March 2014|newspaper=[[Time (magazine)|Time]]|access-date=17 July 2014|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140626122108/http://time.com/33164/michelle-obama-china-beijing-peng-liyuan/|archive-date=26 June 2014}}</ref>\n\nXi and Peng have a daughter named [[Xi Mingze]], who graduated from [[Harvard University]] in the spring of 2015. While at Harvard, she used a pseudonym and studied Psychology and English.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.newyorker.com/news/news-desk/what-did-chinas-first-daughter-find-in-america|title=What Did China's First Daughter Find in America?|last=Osnos|first=Evan|date=6 April 2015|magazine=[[The New Yorker]]|access-date=29 October 2018|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181030035420/https://www.newyorker.com/news/news-desk/what-did-chinas-first-daughter-find-in-america|archive-date=30 October 2018}}</ref> Xi's family has a home in [[Jade Spring Hill]], a garden and residential area in north-western Beijing run by the CMC.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.rfa.org/english/news/china/hundreds-02202015111702.html|title=Beijing Police Detain Hundreds For Trying to Visit Chinese Leaders Over New Year|last=Qiao|first=Long|date=20 February 2015|publisher=[[Radio Free Asia]]|access-date=1 March 2018|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180301164338/https://www.rfa.org/english/news/china/hundreds-02202015111702.html|archive-date=1 March 2018}}</ref>\n\nIn June 2012, ''[[Bloomberg News]]'' reported that members of Xi's extended family have substantial business interests, although there was no evidence he had intervened to assist them.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/2012-06-29/xi-jinping-millionaire-relations-reveal-fortunes-of-elite.html|title=Xi Jinping Millionaire Relations Reveal Fortunes of Elite|last1=Bennett|first1=Amanda|date=29 June 2012|publisher=[[Bloomberg News]]|access-date=11 September 2019|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120704222305/http://www.bloomberg.com/news/2012-06-29/xi-jinping-millionaire-relations-reveal-fortunes-of-elite.html|archive-date=4 July 2012|last2=Hirschberg|first2=Peter}}</ref> The ''Bloomberg'' website was blocked in [[mainland China]] in response to the article.<ref name=\"guardian296122\">{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2012/jun/29/china-bloomberg-xi-jinping|title=China blocks Bloomberg for exposing financial affairs of Xi Jinping's family|last=Branigan|first=Tania|date=29 June 2012|newspaper=[[The Guardian]]|access-date=11 September 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131120041457/http://www.theguardian.com/world/2012/jun/29/china-bloomberg-xi-jinping|archive-date=20 November 2013}}</ref> Since Xi embarked on an anti-corruption campaign, ''[[The New York Times]]'' reported members of his family were selling their corporate and real estate investments beginning in 2012.<ref name=\"nytimes3\">{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2014/06/18/world/asia/chinas-president-xi-jinping-investments.html|title=As China's Leader Fights Graft, His Relatives Shed Assets|last1=Forsythe|first1=Michael|date=17 June 2012|work=[[The New York Times]]|access-date=16 July 2014|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140716105611/http://www.nytimes.com/2014/06/18/world/asia/chinas-president-xi-jinping-investments.html|archive-date=16 July 2014|url-access=registration}}</ref> Relatives of highly placed Chinese officials, including seven current and former senior leaders of the Politburo of the CCP, have been named in the [[Panama Papers]], including [[Deng Jiagui]],<ref>\n{{cite news|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/worldviews/wp/2016/04/04/the-panama-papers-are-super-awkward-for-beijing/|title=The Panama Papers are super awkward for Beijing|last1=Rauhala|first1=Emily|date=4 April 2016|newspaper=[[The Washington Post]]|access-date=7 September 2019|url-status=live|url-access=limited|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160421044242/https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/worldviews/wp/2016/04/04/the-panama-papers-are-super-awkward-for-beijing/|archive-date=21 April 2016}}</ref> Xi's brother-in-law. Deng had two [[Shell corporation|shell companies]] in the [[British Virgin Islands]] while Xi was a member of the Politburo Standing Committee, but they were dormant by the time Xi became general secretary of the CCP in November 2012.<ref name=\"MP2\">{{cite news|url=http://www.marketplace.org/2016/04/04/world/xi-jinpings-family-linked-panama-papers|title=Xi Jinping's family linked to Panama Papers|last=Schmitz|first=Rob|date=4 April 2016|newspaper=[[Marketplace (radio program)|Marketplace]]|access-date=6 April 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160407224017/http://www.marketplace.org/2016/04/04/world/xi-jinpings-family-linked-panama-papers|archive-date=7 April 2016}}</ref>\n\n===Personality===\nPeng described Xi as hardworking and down-to-earth: \"When he comes home, I've never felt as if there's some leader in the house. In my eyes, he's just my husband.\"<ref>{{cite news|url=http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/shared/spl/hi/in_depth/china_politics/leadership/html/6.stm|title=China's Leaders|publisher=[[BBC News]]|access-date=26 August 2013|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130808233513/http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/shared/spl/hi/in_depth/china_politics/leadership/html/6.stm|archive-date=8 August 2013|url-status=live}}</ref> Xi was described in a 2011 ''[[Washington Post]]'' article by those who know him as \"pragmatic, serious, cautious, hard-working, down to earth and low-key\". He was described as a good hand at problem solving and \"seemingly uninterested in the trappings of high office\".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/asia-pacific/xi-jinping-likely-chinas-next-leader-called-pragmatic-low-key/2011/08/15/gIQA5W83GJ_story.html|title=Xi Jinping, likely China's next leader, called pragmatic, low-key|last=Richburg|first=Keith B.|date=15 August 2011|newspaper=[[The Washington Post]]|access-date=7 September 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191029173940/https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/asia-pacific/xi-jinping-likely-chinas-next-leader-called-pragmatic-low-key/2011/08/15/gIQA5W83GJ_story.html|archive-date=29 October 2019|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\n==Public life==\nIt is hard to gauge the opinion of the Chinese public on Xi, as no independent surveys exist in China and social media is heavily censored.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Lin |first=Liza |date=13 October 2022 |title=Do Chinese People Like Xi Jinping? You Won't Find an Easy Answer Online |language=en-US |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/what-do-chinese-people-think-of-xi-jinping-its-very-hard-to-tell-11665664627 |access-date=17 October 2022 |issn=0099-9660}}</ref> However, he is believed to be widely popular in the country.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Phillips |first=Tom |date=14 October 2017 |title=Chairman Xi crushes dissent but poor believe he's making China great |language=en-GB |work=[[The Guardian]] |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2017/oct/14/xi-jinping-crushes-dissent-but-making-china-great-again |url-status=live |access-date=26 August 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190826122356/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2017/oct/14/xi-jinping-crushes-dissent-but-making-china-great-again |archive-date=26 August 2019 |issn=0029-7712}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |last1=Zhou |first1=Christina |last2=Mantesso |first2=Sean |date=6 March 2019 |title='No room for mercy in this system': Xi Jinping's rise from cave dweller to post-modern chairman |language=en-AU |work=[[ABC News (Australia)]] |publisher= |url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2019-03-06/the-astonishing-rise-of-chinese-president-xi-jinping/10794486 |url-status=live |access-date=26 August 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190826051002/https://www.abc.net.au/news/2019-03-06/the-astonishing-rise-of-chinese-president-xi-jinping/10794486 |archive-date=26 August 2019}}</ref> According to a 2014 poll co-sponsored by the [[John F. Kennedy School of Government|Harvard Kennedy School's]] [[Ash Center for Democratic Governance and Innovation]], Xi ranked 9 out of 10 in domestic approval ratings.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://thediplomat.com/2014/12/the-worlds-most-popular-leader-chinas-president-xi/|title=The World's Most Popular Leader: China's President Xi|last=Tiezzi|first=Shannon|date=20 December 2014|newspaper=[[The Diplomat]]|language=en-US|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191027062238/https://thediplomat.com/2014/12/the-worlds-most-popular-leader-chinas-president-xi/|archive-date=27 October 2019|access-date=27 October 2019}}</ref> A [[YouGov]] poll released in July 2019 found that about 22% of people in mainland China list Xi as the person they admire the most, a plurality, although this figure was less than 5% for residents of Hong Kong.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://today.yougov.com/topics/international/articles-reports/2019/07/18/2019-worlds-most-admired|title=Michelle Obama is the world's most admired woman|last=Smith|first=Matthew|date=18 July 2019|website=[[YouGov]]|language=en-us|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190729151150/https://today.yougov.com/topics/international/articles-reports/2019/07/18/2019-worlds-most-admired|archive-date=29 July 2019|access-date=17 August 2019}}</ref> In the spring of 2019, the Pew Research Center made a survey on confidence on Xi Jinping among six-country medians based on Australia, India, Indonesia, Japan, Philippines and South Korea. The survey indicated that a median 29% have confidence in Xi Jinping to do the right thing regarding world affairs, meanwhile a median of 45% have no confidence. These numbers are slightly higher than those of North Korean leader Kim Jong-un (23% confidence, 53% no confidence).<ref>{{cite news |last1=Silver |first1=Laura |last2=Devlin |first2=Kat |last3=Huang |first3=Christine |date=5 December 2019 |title=China's Economic Growth Mostly Welcomed in Emerging Markets, but Neighbors Wary of Its Influence |publisher=[[Pew Research Center]] |url=https://www.pewresearch.org/global/2019/12/05/chinas-economic-growth-mostly-welcomed-in-emerging-markets-but-neighbors-wary-of-its-influence/ |access-date=4 August 2020}}</ref> A poll by [[Politico]] and [[Morning Consult]] in 2021 found that 5% of Americans have a favorable opinion of Xi, 38% unfavorable, 17% no opinion and 40%, a plurality, never hearing of him.<ref>{{Cite web |date=19\u201322 March 2021 |title=National Tracking Poll #2103129 |url=https://www.politico.com/f/?id=00000178-6298-d5c9-ab7c-e79a8aa50000 |access-date=29 August 2022 |website=Morning Consult and Politico}}</ref>\n\nIn 2017, ''The Economist'' named him the most powerful person in the world.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.economist.com/leaders/2017/10/14/xi-jinping-has-more-clout-than-donald-trump-the-world-should-be-wary|title=Xi Jinping has more clout than Donald Trump. The world should be wary|date=14 October 2017|newspaper=[[The Economist]]|access-date=11 September 2019|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190918133802/https://www.economist.com/leaders/2017/10/14/xi-jinping-has-more-clout-than-donald-trump-the-world-should-be-wary|archive-date=18 September 2019|issn=0013-0613|url-access=subscription}}</ref> In 2018, ''[[Forbes]]'' ranked him as [[Forbes list of The World's Most Powerful People|the most powerful and influential person in the world]], replacing [[President of Russia|Russian President]] Vladimir Putin, who had been ranked so for five consecutive years.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/davidewalt/2018/05/08/the-worlds-most-powerful-people-2018/#7e7884216c47|title=The World's Most Powerful People 2018|last1=Ewalt|first1=David M.|date=31 May 2018|work=[[Forbes]]|access-date=7 September 2019|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180509222602/https://www.forbes.com/sites/davidewalt/2018/05/08/the-worlds-most-powerful-people-2018/#7e7884216c47|archive-date=9 May 2018|author-link=David McWalter}}</ref> In 2016 and 2021, [[Reporters Without Borders]], an international non-profit and non-governmental organization with the stated aim of safeguarding the right to freedom of information, included Xi among the list of [[press freedom predators]].<ref>{{cite web |author= |date=2021 |title=Xi Jinping |url=https://rsf.org/en/predator/xi-jinping |access-date=1 November 2021 |publisher=Reporters Without Borders}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |author=Carly Roman |date=6 July 2021 |title=Xi Jinping and Vladimir Putin named among 37 'press freedom predators' |url=https://www.yahoo.com/now/xi-jinping-vladimir-putin-named-180600651.html |access-date=1 November 2021 |via=Yahoo News}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |date=28 October 2016 |title=RSF issues new list of press freedom predators {{pipe}} Reporters without borders |url=https://rsf.org/en/news/rsf-issues-new-list-press-freedom-predators |website=RSF}}</ref>\n\nUnlike previous Chinese leaders, Chinese state media has given a more encompassing view of Xi's private life, although still strictly controlled. According to Xinhua News Agency, Xi would swim one kilometer and walk every day as long as there was time, and is interested in foreign writers, especially Russian.<ref name=\":17\" /> He is known to love films and TV shows such as ''[[Saving Private Ryan]]'', ''[[The Departed]],'' ''[[The Godfather]]'' and ''[[Game of Thrones]],''<ref>{{Cite news |last=Buckley |first=Chris |date=8 February 2012 |title=China leader-in-waiting carries heavy political baggage to U.S. |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-usa-xi-idUSTRE8170FZ20120208 |access-date=29 August 2022}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Buckley |first=Chris |date=15 November 2013 |title=Xi, in 'Godfather' Mold, Looks Assertive and Even Imperial |url=https://archive.nytimes.com/sinosphere.blogs.nytimes.com/2013/11/15/xi-in-godfather-mold-looks-assertive-and-even-imperial/ |access-date=29 August 2022 |website=[[The New York Times]] |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |date=28 April 2019 |title=Xi Jinping shows his love of Game of Thrones but warns reality must not mirror fantasy |work=[[South China Morning Post]]
